Japanese Budget Proposal May Cause Cabinet Strife; Army and Navy Request Huge Sums; Negotiations Underway with Ministry of Finance 37

Tokyo Dispatch - The army and navy budget for 1936-37 may cause strife in the cabinet. Japan's current financial situation urgently requires strict austerity. Therefore, the Ministry of Finance has stipulated that regular expenses are 1,680,000,000 yuan and special expenses are 560,000,000 yuan. Recent developments in China have caused the Army Ministry to insist that new requests for 350,000,000 yuan in the next fiscal year are the absolute minimum. The Ministry of Finance insists that the special expenditures of both the Army and Navy Ministries must be reduced by 50%. The Navy Ministry is also insisting on new requests for 300,000,000 yuan, saying that international dangers may arise after the failure of the London Naval Conference, and preparations must be made early. The new requests from the Army and Navy Ministries total 650,000,000 yuan. The Ministry of Finance has decided that the total amount of new requests from various ministries must not exceed 560,000,000 yuan, and 194,300,000 yuan of that has already been allocated to various ministries. The remaining 365,700,000 yuan is intended to reserve 20,000,000 to 30,000,000 yuan for emergency needs. Therefore, only about 325,700,000 yuan is left to meet the new requests from the Army and Navy Ministries, less than half of what is requested. (Reuters Telegram on the 25th)

(Tokyo) Breaking with the past practice of compiling the budget, the government fully conducted practical negotiations before the budget cabinet meeting in order to seek a solution to the problem. Therefore, the budget cabinet meeting, which was originally scheduled for the 22nd, was postponed to the 25th to allow the Ministry of Finance to continue negotiations with various ministries in the hope of avoiding disputes in the budget cabinet meeting. However, as a result of the negotiations on the 23rd, a final understanding has not yet been reached, centering on the national defense budget. Therefore, the budget cabinet meeting cannot be held on the 25th. Vice Minister of Finance Tsushima and the directors of various bureaus visited Finance Minister Takahashi at his private residence yesterday to report on the progress of the practical negotiations and to state that the budget cabinet meeting must be postponed to the 26th. He wanted to resolve the military budget practically on the 25th. Minister Takahashi expressed his approval. Vice Minister Tsushima and Director Kaya then visited Prime Minister Okada and Chief Secretary Shirane at their official residences to convey the intentions of the financial authorities and request understanding. Prime Minister Okada also acknowledged the postponement, as practical negotiations had already reached this point, and agreed to notify the cabinet members. As a result, the budget cabinet meeting was decided to be held at the Prime Minister's official residence at 10:00 AM on the 26th. As a result, the meeting of the heads of the Ministry of Finance on the 24th was postponed to the 25th, and all negotiations with various ministries must be completed on the 25th so that the original plan can be satisfactorily decided at the cabinet meeting on the 26th. However, in fact, the Ministry of Finance is not allowed to be optimistic, as it has fallen into a state of stagnation. The extent to which the policy of coordinating finances and establishing it has been concretized is particularly noteworthy. The situation of the stagnation of practical negotiations is roughly as follows: (1) The natural increase in revenue for the next year was initially estimated at 83 million yuan. Later, due to the increase in kerosene tariffs and the amendment of the Iron and Steel Industry Law, it is estimated that it can be increased by 10 million yuan, but even this amount cannot satisfy the revival requests of the military and other ministries. On one hand, the Ministry of Finance, which is placing the next year's budget policy on gradual debt reduction, has decided to acknowledge the limit of new requests above the first investigation, with no room for acknowledgement. (2) Regarding the budgets of the Army and Navy Ministries, the investigation can be said to be generous, acknowledging their entire plan and requesting concessions such as annual proportional unit prices. However, the two ministries only acknowledged 330 million yuan of new requests in the first investigation, which is not enough, and their attitude is quite strong. (Dentsu Telegram on the 25th)

Paris and Rome: Winding Diplomacy Continues; Eighteen-Nation Committee Meeting Postponed; Italy Considers Oil Embargo a Serious Matter 38

(Geneva) Today, Mr. Vasconcelos, chairman of the Eighteen-Nation Committee, at the request of French Foreign Minister Laval, announced a postponement of the meeting. While Laval cited the French meeting on Thursday as the reason, this move is quite significant. Delaying the adoption of more severe sanctions against Italy by the League of Nations is, in fact, intended to facilitate diplomatic negotiations. (National Telegram, 25th)

(Geneva) The Eighteen-Nation Committee was originally scheduled to meet on the 29th of this month to decide whether to include items such as kerosene, coal, and iron on the list of embargoed goods against Italy. Now, due to the request from French Prime Minister Laval to postpone the meeting, the League of Nations Secretariat has issued a statement saying that the chairman of the Eighteen-Nation Committee, Vasconcelos, has changed the date of the meeting in accordance with Laval's request, and the date of the meeting will be decided on the 29th of this month. (Havas Telegram, 25th)

(Geneva) The Eighteen-Nation Committee was originally scheduled to meet this Friday. Following discussions between French Prime Minister Laval and British Ambassador Clerk, the meeting has been postponed. It is reported that the French government intends to temporarily avoid expanding the current measures prohibiting the shipment of essential goods to Italy, in order to allow the current sanctions time to take effect. The French government also wants to avoid any actions that could hinder the mediation efforts of the French Prime Minister. People here believe that the most effective sanction the League of Nations can impose on Italy is the cessation of gasoline supplies. It is widely believed that joint action on this matter can be established when the Eighteen-Nation Committee considers expanding the types of goods embargoed against Italy. It is hoped that American oil companies will agree not to increase their exports to Italy when the League of Nations implements a ban on gasoline supplies to Italy. However, there are still difficulties to be resolved. Some countries may argue for giving the current sanctions a longer trial period before adopting new sanctions. Therefore, it is doubtful whether the current embargo can be expanded before the new year. (Reuters Telegram, 25th)

(Rome) The Italian government is reportedly quite satisfied with the decision to postpone the Eighteen-Nation Committee meeting. A government spokesman told a Reuters reporter today that this was the first sensible action taken by Geneva in a long time. However, Italy considers the ban on gasoline shipments to be a major threat. It is reported that the Italian Ambassador to France has notified the French Prime Minister that Italy will view the gasoline ban with grave concern. However, official circles here are unwilling to criticize the matter. According to news from Paris, the Italian Ambassador stated that Italy would consider such a decision an act of war. (Reuters Telegram, 25th)

(Rome) Political figures here declare that negotiations on the Abyssinian issue will be facilitated when the London Naval Conference convenes next month. When the Italian representatives and experts attend the conference, they will thoroughly explain Italy's attitude, namely that Italy's naval policy and the closeness between Italy and France do not imply opposition to Britain. It is also said that Prime Minister Mussolini has been holding talks with British Ambassador to Italy Drummond in recent days, with both sides focusing on psychological aspects. The upcoming naval conference will surely bring things to a practical level. (Havas Telegram, 25th)

The transmission of these instructions was kept unusually secret. It is reported that the scope of Drummond's talks with the Italian Prime Minister was even broader than the recent series of Anglo-Italian talks. Southern Abyssinian Army Launches Sudden Attack, Morale Boosted; Italian Army in the North Shows No Sign of Continued Offensive 39

(London) The sudden attack by the Abyssinian army in southeastern Ogaden Province has changed the situation of the war in that area and attracted general attention. According to a Reuters correspondent stationed in the Abyssinian capital, Harar, the Abyssinian army is advancing rapidly along the Fafan River, recovering the land seized by Italian mechanized troops last week. The Abyssinian army had repeatedly suffered defeats, and morale was low, but since the Abyssinian Emperor encouraged the soldiers on the southern front, morale has greatly increased. According to a Reuters correspondent at the Italian army headquarters in Asmara, the Italian army in the north shows no sign of continuing its offensive. This is not only due to the change of commander-in-chief but also because it is urgently necessary to consolidate the captured positions and pacify the people. The Italian army is now holding a key-shaped line hundreds of miles long with 150,000 troops, starting from Sudan and reaching Addis Adassie, then bypassing Addis Filla, Bethlehem Mountain, Dantra, and Asbi. The telegram also stated that Mussolini's son-in-law, Galeazzo Ciano, received a silver medal for his meritorious service in the aerial attacks last week. According to a Reuters military correspondent in Mogadishu, the former Italian envoy to Abyssinia, Count Vinci, returned to Abyssinia from Italy to command a squadron of field artillery. Addis Ababa. The news of the Abyssinian army's victory circulating everywhere cannot be confirmed today, as most of this news is based on reports from generals on the northern front. U.S. Attitude: Equivalent to De Facto Sanctions; Romanian Merchants Unwilling to Ban Oil 40

(Washington) The United States is still striving to prevent all wartime trade with belligerent nations. This move is tantamount to implementing unofficial sanctions against Italy, as the United States has no dealings with Abyssinia. Although officials here have repeatedly stated that the United States' neutral actions have no direct relationship with the League of Nations' sanctions and have strongly asserted that the United States' plans are not influenced by other governments or the League of Nations, in fact, various government departments are fully cooperating with the State Department to prevent the export of all war supplies. It is also learned that Secretary of State Hull has begun investigating the quantity of cotton exported to Italy after the arms embargo order was issued on October 5. If there is an abnormal increase, the government may implement a ban. (National Telegram, 24th)

(Rome) Officials here today are deeply concerned that the neutral actions taken by the U.S. government will hinder Italy's struggle against the League of Nations' sanctions. A Foreign Ministry spokesman stated that Italy's relations with the United States have always been "very friendly," but if the United States prohibits the shipment of kerosene to Italy, it will be regarded as a "hostile" action. If the prohibition is implemented, Italy will inevitably take corresponding countermeasures. At the same time, the general Italian people do not seem to be feeling the impact of the League of Nations' economic encirclement today. (National Telegram, 24th)

Bucharest. Romanian oil companies have recently submitted a petition to the government, stating that for the sake of Romania's own interests, kerosene should be allowed to continue to be shipped to Italy. The price of goods can no longer be paid through remittance methods, but can be paid directly in lira, or other methods can be agreed upon with Italian import merchants. In 1935, the quantity of Romanian kerosene shipped to Italy totaled 1.5 million tons, accounting for a quarter of Romania's total kerosene exports. Now that the sanctions have been implemented, Italy can no longer use barter methods and will inevitably use cash to purchase kerosene from the United States. (Havas Telegram, 24th)

(Berlin) The National Socialist Party's organ, the Political Economy Magazine, recently published an article on the impact of sanctions against Italy on international trade, stating that the world's economic structure will be completely shaken by the implementation of sanctions against Italy. For example, India, Argentina, Australia, and South Africa will be more affected by the sanctions than other countries, and they will inevitably seek other customers to compensate for the loss of their Italian markets. The longer the sanctions are implemented, the more difficult it will be for international trade to return to normal. As for Czechoslovakia and Estonia, a large part of their coal and kerosene production is sold to Italy. In addition, the production of manganese, ferromanganese, pig iron, and tin has always been entirely dependent on the countries currently participating in the sanctions. If trade is interrupted one day, the countries participating in the sanctions will inevitably seek other sales channels, and Italy will also seek supplies from other countries. If this is the case, whether the countries participating in the sanctions will be able to restore their old trade relations with Italy after the sanctions are lifted is questionable. (Havas Telegram, 24th)

Britain and France Secretly Discuss Reorganizing the League of Nations' Organization; Specifically Requesting Germany, the United States, and Japan to Join; Redistributing Global Colonies 41

(Tokyo) French representative Laval and British representative Hoare, taking advantage of the meeting of the Sanctions Adjustment Committee in Geneva a few days ago, repeatedly discussed reorganizing the League of Nations, requesting Germany, the United States, and Japan to rejoin, in order to reform the current state of the League of Nations. They plan to redistribute global colonies, establishing several groups of peaceful areas, each under mutual security guarantees, without aggression, in order to maintain the power of the alliance's powers for a long time. France's condition is to seek Britain's recognition of the meaning of the Locarno Treaty and to guarantee the borders of the Rhineland. Britain's condition is to require France to temporarily refrain from signing the Franco-Soviet mutual assistance treaty and to allow the annexation of Austria by Germany. The movement to reorganize the League of Nations is still underway in secret. (China United Press Telegram, 25th)

US Far East Trade: Exports to Japan Exceed Those to China by Three Times; Commercial Concepts Tend to Adjust 42

(Washington) Currently, the United States' trade with Japan is more than three times that with China. Therefore, the United States' commercial concepts regarding the Far East also need to be adjusted. From a strictly financial point of view, transactions with Japan are far more profitable than those with China. However, the United States' commercial concepts have always maintained their friendly sympathy towards China, so the U.S. government is also unwilling to abandon its historically deep-rooted Far East policy. If the relationship between the United States and Japan continues to expand, it may be necessary to reconsider the United States' Far East economic policy. Formal statistics obtained by the Associated Press show that the trend in the U.S. economy has shifted sharply from China to Japan since the global recession. In the five years from 1926 to 1930, U.S. exports to Japan averaged US$245,036,000 per year. In 1932, it fell to US$134,921,000, and in 1934, it recovered to US$210,420,000. In the first eight months of this year, it was US$115,870,000. Exports to China averaged US$109,021,000 per year from 1926 to 1930. In 1933, it fell to US$51,942,000. The following year was slightly better, but it was only US$68,632,000. In the first eight months of this year, it was only US$26,659,000, which is less than a quarter of that of Japan. On the import side, Japan averaged US$379,632,000 per year before 1930. Subsequently, it fell to US$119,251,000 in 1934. In the first eight months of this year, it was US$94,339,000, indicating that the total for this year will improve again. China's early average was US$140,306,000. In 1932, it fell to US$26,177,000. Two years later, it recovered to US$43,933,000. In the first eight months of this year, it also reached US$41,690,000. Although the situation has improved significantly compared to last year, it is still less than half of that of Japan. (National Telegram, 24th)

(Paris) Since the Bank of France issued its weekly report last Tuesday, large amounts of gold have continued to flow out of the country. It is generally estimated that since November 14, more than 10 billion francs of gold have flowed out of the country. The government will officially announce this figure on Sunday. It is expected that the amount of gold and silver currency reserves listed in the Bank of France's weekly report will fall from 70 billion francs to 69 billion francs. When the government legally stabilized the franc on June 25, 1928, the Bank of France's gold reserves were only 29 billion francs. By the end of 1934, its total gold reserves reached 82 billion francs, the highest amount of gold reserves in history. The Provincial Government Water Disaster Relief Committee believes that the disaster situation is severe and there are too many embankment breaches, which is still insufficient for distribution, and has telegraphed the Central Government again to increase the allocation. It is requesting Zhang Qun and He Chengjun to make nearby requests. (Special Telegram, 25th)

Measures to Dredge Accumulated Water in Northern Anhui 60

(Nanjing) Regarding measures to dredge accumulated water in northern Anhui into the sea, the National Economic Committee and the Jiangsu Construction Department, after discussions, have decided on the following: 1. Dredge the waterways of the Wutu River and Taiguan River; 2. Dredge the Chezhou River section; 3. Dredge the waterways of Banpu, Zhongzheng East, Xin, and Shanhou Rivers; 4. Dredge the old Shaoxiang River; 5. Reorganize the new Shaoxiang River. The total cost for the above five items is estimated at 550,000 yuan. Implementation methods and fundraising are being coordinated by the committee with the Salt Affairs Audit Office and the Jiangsu Construction Department. Consultant Pu Deli, representatives from the Salt Affairs Audit Office Zhu Shicen, representative from the Construction Department Guan Fuquan, and the Magistrate of Guanyun County Xu Xie Kui will jointly go to the site for actual investigation. (Special Dispatch of the 25th)

Former President Li to be Given a State Funeral in Hubei, Over 50,000 Chinese and Foreign Dignitaries Attend, Chairman Lin Sends Li Shucheng as the Chief Celebrant 64

Hankou Correspondence: The coffins of former President Li and Madam Wu, transported from Tianjin in the 22nd year [of the Republic, i.e., 1933], have been temporarily placed in the Baotong Temple on Hongshan Mountain in Wuchang. His sons, Shaoji and Shaoye, found a cemetery on Nan Shi Gong Mountain in Zhuodaoquan. The National Government, in recognition of his meritorious service, decided to grant him a state funeral, scheduled for November 24th of this year. At 8:00 AM on that day, the funeral procession gathered at various wharves in Wuchang, and vehicles were dispatched by the Funeral Affairs Office to transport them. Attendees included: National Government Representative Li Shucheng, Executive Yuan Representative Jia Shiyi, Examination Yuan Representative Cheng Qibao, Judicial Yuan Representative Shi Yangan, Control Yuan Representative Wang Huai, Ministry of Interior Representative Meng Guangpeng, Ministry of Navy Representative Chen Wumin, Ministry of Communications Representative Gao Tingzi, Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission Representative Xiao Yang, Central Relief Committee Representative He Hengfu, Hunan Provincial Government Representative Hu Kuihuai, Hubei Provincial Government Representative Lu Zhu, Ningxia Provincial Government Representative Tong Binqiu, Qingdao Municipal Government Representative Shen Zhaonian, Hu Zongduo’s Representative Yan Jing, Audit Department Representative Ren Yingzhong, Li Liejun’s Representative Ding Lizhong, Zhang Guogan’s Representative Zhang Chuancong, former Premier Li Genyuan, former Minister of Education Peng Yunyi, Sun Wu, a hero of the Wuchang Uprising, as well as various agencies, organizations, schools, relatives, subordinates, and the general public of this province, totaling over 50,000 people. All consuls stationed in Hankou from the countries of England, America, Italy, France, Germany, Holland, Japan, Norway, Portugal, Spain, Belgium, and Denmark participated. The British and Japanese consuls were also representing the British Ambassador and the Japanese Foreign Ministry, respectively. At 11:00 AM, a memorial service was first held at Hongshan Fajie Palace, with National Government Representative Li Shucheng as the chief celebrant, and Jia Shiyi, Cheng Qibao, Shi Yancheng, and Chen Jicheng as accompanying celebrants. After the presentation of flowers and the playing of music, the eulogy of Chairman Lin of the National Government was read. The original text reads: "On this 24th day of November in the 24th year of the Republic of China, Lin Sen, Chairman of the National Government, hereby specially appoints Li Shucheng, member of the Hubei Provincial Government, to respectfully offer incense and pay tribute to the spirit of former President Li, saying: 'Alas, the righteous spirit of the universe, the heroic spirit of mountains and seas, has been gathering for decades, and heroes have emerged. The vast Jianghan, the record of the southern country. You, our lord, rose in response to the times. Storms and hardships, winds and clouds gathered. The banner of Han was raised, and hundreds of cities followed. You welcomed the enlightened pioneer, and did not seek great achievements. You guarded Jingxiang, and were looked up to from afar. The position of the nation was in crisis, and the founding was renewed. You held fast to virtue and accepted the mandate of heaven. Your virtue and capacity were consistent in danger and ease. You righted the wrongs and finally extended great righteousness. You again held the reins of power, with generosity and gentleness, regarding the people as wounded. Your benevolent grace flowed everywhere. The tripod ascended to the heavens, and you passed away eight years ago. People from home and abroad have returned to benevolence, and praises and thoughts have not ceased. Images are cast in bronze, and tears are left on the stele. You protected the people and supported the country, ascending and descending in this world, carrying on the cause of the Yellow Emperor, and your achievements hang down on the nation. We revere virtue and repay merit, and the ceremonies should be generous. The clouds of Chu are luxuriant, and the trees of Han are green. A fine tomb is laid, and the flesh is consumed without end. May you enjoy this sacrifice.’" After the sacrifice, a 19-gun salute was fired, and the coffin was moved down the mountain. The funeral procession consisted of eight rows: the first row was a six-member artillery unit of cavalry vanguard, with the party and national flags leading the way; the second row was the police band and a company of police infantry; the third row was the navy; the fourth row was the Wuhan Municipal Public Security Bureau band and special police from the provincial capital Public Security Bureau; the fifth row was the Thirteenth Division band, representatives from party, government, military, and police agencies from various provinces and cities, representatives from various agencies and organizations within the province, and patrol infantry; the sixth row was representatives from central ministries and commissions and the heads of this province; the seventh row was the coffin, followed by the family; the eighth row was cavalry as the rearguard. The procession was three miles long, an unprecedented spectacle. In Wuchang, the weather had been clear and warm for the past two days, unlike winter. Today, it suddenly changed to severe cold, with bitter rain and a dismal wind, as if mourning for this founding hero. However, the pallbearers braved the rain, walking in an orderly manner, and the order remained extremely disciplined. Along the route, there were many roadside sacrifices, which showed that the love left behind remained in people's hearts. At 2:00 PM, the coffin arrived at the vegetable field in Zhuodaoquan. In front of the cemetery was Chairman Lin's inscription "Founding Hero of the Republic," below which was a portrait of President Li, flanked by elegiac couplets from various circles, with many excellent compositions. At 3:00 PM, the state funeral ceremony was held, with a 101-gun salute. Li Shucheng was still the chief celebrant, and representatives from all the central ministries and commissions and foreign guests were accompanying celebrants. After the ceremony, the coffin was respectfully placed in the tomb, and a great man of an era was finally laid to rest underground. After the burial, representatives from all circles and the public paid their highest respects. The state funeral was thus completed. On this day, the entire nation, following the order of the National Government, flew flags at half-mast to mourn for President Li and suspended entertainment. The honor after death was second only to that of President Sun. Attached is a brief biography of Li: Li's ancestral home was Huangpi, born in Hanyang in the Jiazi year of the Tongzhi reign [1864]. His father, Zhao Xiang, served as a guerrilla officer in the Beiyang training army, stationed in Beitang. In the Guiwei year of the Guangxu reign [1883], Li studied at the Tianjin Beiyang Naval Academy. After graduating, he served in the navy. In the Sino-Japanese War, he served as the engineer officer on the Guangjia warship. Transferred from Guangzhou to Weihai, the ship was made of wood and not suitable for combat. The captain bravely participated in the battle. When the ship was surrounded, the captain left on a small boat. Li refused to be captured by the enemy and jumped into the sea. He nearly drowned, but finally swam to Dalian. Of the twelve who went with him, only four survived. Li mourned the defeat of the Green Standard Army and knew that without thorough academic research and practical combat preparation, it would be impossible to resist the enemy and avenge the shame. When Zhang Wenxiang supervised the Nanyang and built new fortresses in Jiangnan, it was difficult to find suitable candidates. Hearing of Li's talent and military knowledge, he summoned him and was impressed by his ability. He then ordered him to supervise the construction of the fortresses on Jinling, Jiangyin, and Shilang Mountains, all of which were solid and moderate in size. He then accompanied the governor of Huguang and, together with a German, trained the Hubei New Army. He went to Japan three times to investigate military affairs, spending a year and a half in the East Ocean. He served as the commander of the Hubei Guard Cavalry, the commander of the Vanguard Battalion, the associate commander of the Second Brigade, and the commander of the brigade. He was also appointed commander of the 21st Mixed Brigade, concurrently managing the cavalry, artillery, engineering, and supply teams, and supervising the two arsenals for weapons and gunpowder, and supervising the Wuchang Middle School, co-organizing the Special Army School, and commanding six Chu-type warships and four Hu-type torpedo boats. In the Bingwu year [1906], at the military maneuvers in Zhangde, he served as the commander of the Hubei army. Li was diligent, honest, frugal, and strict and benevolent in governing the army. He not only used military tactics to control them but also encouraged them with great righteousness. Everyone submitted to him. At the end of the Qing Dynasty, the government was corrupt and used petty people. Rui Cheng, the governor of Hubei, was particularly hasty and tried to harm Li. At the time of the Wuchang Uprising, it was launched in haste, and the entire city had no leader. The revolutionary army and the members of the Advisory Bureau unanimously elected Li as the Grand Governor of the Hubei Army Government of the Republic of China. Li declined modestly but could not refuse. He then made an agreement to prohibit wanton killing and temporarily maintained local security in the name of the military leader, with the aim of letting the entire nation resolve national affairs. After obtaining unanimous agreement, he took office. The whole province cheered, and the situation was stabilized. Li then calmly responded to changes, without showing any emotion. He occupied Hanyang and Xiaokou, deployed military forces to prepare for battle, and sent personnel to negotiate with the consuls of various countries stationed in Hankou, who unanimously recognized them as belligerent groups. As a result, various provinces responded one after another and sent representatives to elect Li as the Grand General of the Central Army and Navy. At that time, Huang Xing came to Hankou and proposed establishing a government. Li considered military affairs to be urgent and appointed Huang to be solely responsible for military affairs. Although Hanyang was lost, Nanjing was fortunately captured. After the armistice, representatives from various provinces gathered in Shanghai and elected President Sun and Li as the provisional president and vice president. The Nanjing government was established. President Sun ceded the presidency to Yuan Shikai, and the provisional senate again appointed Yuan and Li as the provisional president and vice president. At that time, the central authority was not yet stable, and the provinces were uneasy. Li overcame difficulties and looked forward to the hope of the world. Li saw that the power of the military governors was too great and feared that it would lead to the disaster of feudal lords, which would hinder national unity. Therefore, he advocated the separation of military and civilian affairs and took the lead in disbanding troops, setting an example for the world. Of the ten divisions of the Hubei army, seven were disbanded, and they were given funds to return to farming. He also ordered that civilian finances and administration be returned to the civil affairs chief, advocated judicial independence, and strictly prohibited opium, so that planting and transportation disappeared. The new policies at the beginning of the Republic were extremely prosperous for a time. In the second year of the Republic [1913], the Song case occurred, and Jiangxi declared independence, followed by Hunan. Li was promoting unification and using the Mediation Association. He was formally elected vice president and resigned from his position as military governor of Hubei to enter the capital. When the Preparatory Society for the Restoration of the Monarchy arose and the Hongxian regime was about to be established, Li resigned from his concurrent posts as Director of the Council of State and Chief of the General Staff, withdrew from Yingtai, and refused the false title of Prince Wuyi. People wore mourning clothes in protest. After Yuan's death, Li legally succeeded as president in June of the fifth year [1916], restored the Provisional Constitution, convened the National Assembly, and changed the presidential system to a cabinet system. The cabinet members were all leading figures from various parties and did not use a single private individual. When the participation in the war and the loan issues arose, there were disagreements between the presidential palace and the cabinet. The cabinet sought foreign aid to restrain the presidential palace, which led to the Xuzhou Conference. The military governors gathered in the capital and requested the dissolution of the National Assembly. Zhang Xun, advocating peace, entered Beijing, attempting to restore the monarchy. Li, unwilling to see the country fall apart, temporarily suspended the National Assembly to abolish the military governors' group's independence. When Zhang Xun restored the monarchy, Li reappointed Duan Qirui as the premier of the State Council and commander-in-chief of the expedition against the rebels. The remnants secretly ordered Li to go to Tianjin. The next day, he went to live in the Eastern Legation Quarter and sent the presidential seal to Duan, ordering him to hand it over to Vice President Feng. Then, he telegraphed his resignation. When the rebellion was suppressed, Duan, as the leader, earnestly requested Li to resume his post. Li resolutely refused and went to live in Tianjin. During the constitutional protection movement, the north and south confronted each other. Public opinion considered the restoration of the constitutional system as the key to resolving the situation. In the eleventh year [1922], the Beiyang generals invited Li to resume his post. Li refused firmly, so the abolition of military governors and the disbandment of troops were the main points of agreement, and the various frontier officials responded rashly. National legal organizations also unanimously urged him to proceed, so he entered the capital alone, rescinded the order issued in the sixth year [1917] under duress from the military governors' group and the leaders of the restoration to dissolve the National Assembly, so that the members of both houses of parliament resumed their posts. Li considered that the country's chaos was due to the lack of a constitution, so he urged the establishment of a constitution as a matter of great urgency, while those with ulterior motives, on the contrary, were plotting to consolidate their positions. Thereupon, they committed acts of insubordination and rebellion, forcing the presidential palace and the residence to be surrounded, and Li fled back to Tianjin. On the way, the bizarre drama of robbing the car and stealing the seal was staged, and from this, bribery elections were rampant, and the National Assembly went bankrupt. During his two terms as president, Li did not raise foreign debts or seek foreign aid, and none of his subordinates were personal soldiers, and none of his subordinates were private factions. He was not alarmed by great changes or afraid of great difficulties. After resigning, he lived in seclusion in Tianjin and died of illness on June 3 of the seventeenth year [1928]. On his deathbed, he still thought of national affairs. (24th)

Gold and Silver

English Gold: The London gold price today is 140 shillings 11 and a half pence, up half a penny.

English Silver: The London silver market is quiet. The spot price is unchanged at 29 and 1875 pence. Futures fell by 0.0625 to 28 and 75 pence. The U.S. purchased, while India and speculators sold. The market is stable.

Exchange Rates

British-American: The London foreign exchange market was quiet this morning. The British pound price against the U.S. dollar has continued to rise. The opening price for the British-American exchange rate was $4.938125, 0.0625 lower than the closing price on Saturday. It fell by 0.025 within the first hour, then rebounded by 0.0125 to $4.936875. Cotton and Wheat

American Cotton: The New York cotton market generally trended upward after opening, due to the stability of overseas markets, reassuring statements from public storage agencies, and the firmness of the securities market. However, the price slightly weakened during power generation hours.

American Wheat: The Chicago wheat market's trading was slightly uneven. The opening price weakened, then firmed due to better news from Argentina. However, the price fell slightly again due to a lack of buyers. Coarse grains opened slightly higher, but the general trend turned downward afterward.

Rubber

New York: Rubber opened slightly lower because merchants are waiting for the results of the upcoming rubber production restriction conference and are not buying. After falling 0.08 pounds, there was not much fluctuation.

Securities: The New York stock market was stable this morning. Securities prices mostly rose. Metal stocks are still flat, but steel stocks are lagging. Public utility stocks are slightly uneven. Automobile stocks rose slightly due to some demand. The Dow Jones average of 30 industrial stocks opened at 146.58, up 0.46 pounds.

After Li Zongren Returns to Guangxi, the Exchange Rate Between Silver and Paper Money is Determined, and Measures for Punishing Cash Transactions are Promulgated 66

Guangzhou Correspondence: Since Guangxi Province promulgated currency management regulations, the Guangxi Provincial Government recently stipulated the exchange rate between silver dollars and Guangxi paper money to avoid disputes in the market. The exchange rates are set as follows: (1) One silver dollar is worth 1.20 Guangxi paper money; (2) One silver dollar is worth 1.44 Guangxi paper money; (3) One tael of pure silver (new衡市 scale) is worth 1.67 Guangxi paper money, and one tael (old scale) is worth 2 Guangxi paper money; (4) One tael of pure gold (new scale) is worth 150 Guangxi paper money, and one tael (old scale) is worth 180 Guangxi paper money. Since the prohibition of silver dollars in circulation, anyone found privately transporting silver dollars out of the province, in amounts of 20 yuan or less, will be allowed to exchange them for legal tender. Amounts exceeding 20 yuan will be confiscated. If cash is found, regardless of the amount, it will be confiscated and dealt with according to the law. Since silver dollars cannot circulate in the market, the demand for legal tender has increased sharply. The provincial government has telegraphed foreign countries to order the printing of legal tender and, at the same time, the Guangxi Bank will issue more subsidiary coins to provide relief. The issued subsidiary coins are divided into 1 jiao, 2.5 jiao, and 5 jiao denominations. Subsequently, market transactions and accounts will be based on legal tender. If transactions are still conducted in silver, they will be handled in accordance with the Measures for Punishing Cash Transactions. The punishment measures are divided into six items: (1) For all public and private payments and collections of debts, if the use of silver coins or raw gold and silver is discovered, in addition to confiscating the original items, both the payer and the receiver will be fined up to 1,000 yuan. However, for all contracts stipulated with silver coins as the standard before the promulgation of the currency management measures in this province, they should be paid with provincial banknotes on the due date according to the original amount; (2) In all parts of the province, except for areas where banknotes have not yet been circulated, if merchants or people are found to be trading or buying and selling with silver coins or raw gold and silver in the market, once discovered, in addition to confiscating the original items, they will be punished according to the previous article; (3) In areas of the province where banknotes are circulating or have not been circulated, if silver coins or raw gold and silver are carried or transported out of the province without government approval, once discovered, in addition to confiscating the original items, they will all be fined up to 500 yuan; (4) In areas of the province where banknotes are circulating or have not been circulated, if silver coins or raw gold and silver are carried or transported out of the provincial border without government approval, the punishment methods are as follows: (A) Those who hide them in other goods, hoping to deceive and smuggle them out of the province for personal gain, once discovered, in addition to confiscating the original items, will be punished by doubling the amount seized; (B) Those who completely transport large amounts of silver coins or raw gold and silver out of the province, intending to sabotage the financial system, once found to be true, will be sentenced to death in accordance with the Emergency Law for Punishing Crimes Against the Republic of China, and those who transport them on behalf of others will also be punished; (5) In areas of the province where banknotes are not circulating, if silver coins or raw gold and silver are carried or transported to areas where banknotes are circulating, when discovered, the bank will purchase them at the current price, and in addition to returning the original amount to the owner, the excess amount will be awarded as a reward; (6) Those who violate the currency management measures of this province, all merchants and people may report them, and 50% of the confiscated items and fines will be awarded to the whistleblower, 10% will be used as operating expenses for the executing agency, and the remaining 40% will be deposited into the treasury. The currency management situation in Guangxi Province is roughly the same as in Guangdong Province. As for the political aspect, Bai Chongxi recently telegraphed Li Zongren to return to Guangxi to discuss everything. Li then departed from Guangzhou on the 13th of this month with his wife Guo Dejie and bodyguards. On that day, he took the Guangzhou-Sanshui train to Sanshui, and then transferred to the Jiangning steamer in Hekou to go west. He arrived in Wuzhou on the 14th, rested in Wuzhou for one day, and took the Haizhu motorboat to Guixian on the 14th evening, and then transferred to Nanning.

Repeated Confiscations of Silver on the Ships Traveling Between Taiwan and Xiamen 67

Over 5,000 Yuan Seized on the "Guangdong Maru," Over 2,000 Yuan Seized on the "Fengshan Maru"

Xiamen Correspondence: After the government strictly prohibited the export of silver, there are still many smugglers. On the 20th of this month, the Japanese ship "Guangdong Maru" was about to leave Xiamen for Taiwan. Customs officers on the ship searched the passengers and found 500 silver dollars on a passenger named Pan Zaiwu. They also found silver bars worth over 5,000 yuan in the luggage of various passengers. They were all taken to the customs and transferred to the Central Bank for storage. A separate document was prepared to send Pan Zaiwu to the court for interrogation. Furthermore, some days ago, when the Japanese ship "Fengshan Maru" was about to depart, the customs officers found over 2,000 silver dollars in a rice jar in the crew's cabin. When the ship entered the port on the 12th, the customs negotiated with the shipowner, wanting to impose a penalty according to the customs regulations, because the silver was stored in a locked cabin, and the shipowner could not avoid a certain responsibility. After negotiation, the ship sent the cabin manager Zheng Peisen to the customs for processing. The ship's chief mate testified that Zheng was involved. After interrogation, he was sent to the Public Security Bureau for handling. The Japanese Consulate in Xiamen, at the request of the Xiamen Customs, posted a notice on the Japanese ships traveling between Taiwan and Xiamen, strictly prohibiting the smuggling of silver. Since then, the customs inspection has been strict and female inspectors have been hired specifically to search women's hidden items. Generally, smugglers use women to carry silver, but it is difficult to ensure foolproof. Therefore, they have changed their strategy, but female passengers still carry silver. Those who are caught are caught, and those who smuggle still smuggle. Those who are caught are few, and those who smuggle are many. It is said that the customs has slightly noticed this and will add more female inspectors to be more thorough and avoid corruption (November 23).

Songjiang: All Fire Brigade Members Reinstated 68

The members of the fire brigades in the first, second, third, and fourth districts of this county resigned in anger because Yao Chongfu and Li Duanzhi, members of the first district, were suddenly framed in the case of the fire at the former Songhui Amusement Park, and they returned their uniforms and hats to the fire brigade association to show their determination. As a result, the promotion of fire fighting was invisibly suspended, but the members still bravely rescued people at the fire scene, which was deeply appreciated by the local people. Magistrate Li, from the moment he took office, knew the enthusiasm of the fire brigade members in this county. He and the county party department sincerely persuaded the members to return to their posts in order to promote the soundness of the fire brigade during this winter fire prevention period. They urgently asked them to consider their obligations to their hometowns and restore the original situation. The members were very moved. Therefore, on the 25th, representatives from the County Public Security Bureau, the First District Office, and the County Chamber of Commerce sent the uniforms of the members of each district back to them. The president and vice president of the fire brigade association and all the members have accepted them. It is heard that the fire brigades are scheduled to establish a fire brigade on the first day to assist in winter fire prevention. The next day, the whole team will gather at the small training ground to check the machinery and equipment and reorganize them.

Public Security Bureau Detectives Seize Stolen Goods 69

Yang Shijie, the captain of the detective team of the County Public Security Bureau, received a tip-off that the bandit gang that robbed the buses on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Highway was hiding in the house of Xia Xianggen, in the second Jia of the sixth Bao of Hutang Township, Caojing. He led the detectives to the site yesterday. However, the bandits had a lookout. After the bandits were notified, they fled through the back window. The detectives chased them in the dark, but the bandits removed the small wooden bridge, making it impossible to cross. When they arrived at Xia Xianggen's house, they entered the room and saw that the candles were still lit and the ground was covered with cigarette butts, proving that there was a gathering beforehand. They then found three silk-lined long gowns and a gold watch, which were lost by the bus passengers. They have already been taken back and presented to the case, and the escaped bandits are still being strictly hunted.

Changshu: Changes to the Timetable of the Xihu Bus 70

The Xihu Bus Company has recently changed the bus timetable again due to the climate and time. It is scheduled to be implemented today (26th). From now on, there will be four round trips between Xihu every day. There will be five buses from Changshu to Shanghai every day and six buses to Xihu. There will be six round trips between Suchang every day. The time in the morning is slightly later. The first bus to Xihu and Suzhou is at 7:00 AM. The first bus to Shanghai is at 8:35 AM. The evening buses are earlier than before. The Suzhou-Xihu buses are all at 4:05 PM. The bus to Shanghai is scheduled for 2:35 PM.

Suzhou: Arrest of Wujin Poison Pill Offender 71

The Wu County Public Security Bureau has been making every effort to search for drug offenders. Recently, a person named Jia Deyu from Anhui was caught for privately manufacturing poison pills. Previously, he had been secretly manufacturing red pills in Changzhou on a relatively large scale, which was discovered by the Wujin County Public Security Bureau. The offender immediately fled without a trace, and was not captured. The Wu County Public Security Bureau received a tip-off, saying that the fugitive was hiding at the residence of a Mr. Wang at No. 2 Xiaochebian outside Banmen, Suzhou. They immediately ordered Inspector Cui of the Third Branch Station to lead police officers to arrest Jia Deyu, who was taken to the branch bureau. On the 25th, he was transferred to the Public Security Bureau to await consultation with the Wujin Public Security Bureau, who will dispatch police officers to Suzhou to escort him back to Changzhou to face investigation and trial.

Wuxi: Strike of Shops in Beiqifang Town 72

Beiqifang Town, in the ninth district of the county, experienced a dispute on the afternoon of the previous day due to an investigation of smugglers bribing fugitives. As a result, all the shops in the town went on strike. After detailed investigation, the cause was found to be quite complex. It turns out that in August of this year, a boat carrying smuggled salt arrived in the town and was sold door-to-door. A local rogue named Hua Aliu, falsely using the name of a merchant team leader, extorted over a hundred yuan and allowed them to leave. Afterwards, the people of the town reported to the mountain anti-smuggling camp, which arrested Wang Baorong and Hua Yusheng, who were selling smuggled salt, and transferred them to the court for interrogation and detention. However, Hua Aliu was on the run and had not been apprehended. Recently, he returned to his hometown. The court received the news and dispatched bailiffs to the town to arrest him the day before yesterday. They first ordered Gao Sandu, the head of the village, to monitor him. Aliu then colluded with his elder brother Afive, luring Sandu to the Hua Yulin pharmacy. A group of ruffians, along with Alius mother and sister-in-law, surrounded and beat Gao Sandu, allowing Aliu to escape. Afterwards, they turned their anger on Gao Hongchou, the local bao head. Gao Hongchou, unwilling to show weakness, caused a disturbance for a long time. Gao Hongchou then closed the doors of his own Gao Litai cloth shop as a show of protest. Hua Afive and the group of ruffians had already coerced all the shops in the town to go on strike. The disturbance continued into the night and had not been resolved. The village head, Gao Sandu, went to the city yesterday morning to the court to have his injuries examined and to request the arrest and punishment of the perpetrators. The town head also persuaded the shops in the town to resume business.

Large-Scale Speculators Buying Silver Coins 73

Since the Ministry of Finance stipulated that the banknotes of the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications are legal tender and stopped the use of silver, speculators in various places have been buying silver dollars in the market. In recent days, speculators have been found in this county exchanging one yuan and one jiao in legal tender for one silver dollar from various small money changers. Some ignorant merchants, greedy for profit, are exchanging their silver coins one after another. It is reported that the purchased silver will be secretly sold to someone for a large profit. Now, silver coins in the market are worth as much as one yuan and three jiao in legal tender each. According to people in the financial industry, nearly ten thousand yuan in silver has flowed out of Wuxi County. However, there is not much silver in the market, so it is not easy for general speculators to buy it. At this time, when the whole country is uniformly implementing the new currency system, these speculators are exchanging large amounts of silver in the market, which is harmful to the Republic of China. It is hoped that the local authorities of this county will strictly investigate and prohibit it.

Provincial Commissioner Investigates Corruption in Reporting Drought 74

Chen Yuji, the grain scribe with the "Chen" character number in Qianqiao Town, the fourth district of the county, engaged in corruption and profiteering when reporting drought-stricken fields last year. He also demanded drought reporting fees from farmers, with the larger amount being three yuan per mu and the smaller amount being four or five jiao. After citizen Ling Kunsheng and others investigated and confirmed the facts, they filmed the evidence and submitted it to the Department of Finance, requesting the dispatch of personnel to investigate thoroughly. According to the report, the Department of Finance dispatched personnel secretly to the town yesterday to investigate the truth in conjunction with the town head Mao Liang and the bao heads Du Hesheng and Zhi Jiqing, and reported to the department for strict handling.

The Truth about the Surrender of Abyssinian Chieftain Gugsa 76

— Special Dispatch

The Abyssinian chieftain Gugsa has surrendered to Italy, which may have significant consequences, as Gugsa is not only a commander in the Abyssinian army, but also the son-in-law of the emperor and the governor of the important eastern Tigre province. He is one of the two surviving leaders of the dynasty, and he and his cousin Seyoum, the governor of the western Tigre province, are both descendants of Emperor John, who was usurped by King Menelik of Shoa. In the past sixty years, the relationship between Shoa and Tigre has been very similar to the relationship between England and Scotland in the sixteenth century, while Italy has taken the position of France, supporting the Stuarts against England, with frequent battles and reconciliations. Reconciliations were mostly achieved through marriage, just as Henry VII married his daughter Margaret to James IV of Scotland. Menelik married his daughter Zewditu to the son of Emperor John, but unfortunately, this son died before inheriting the throne, so the alliance between the two dynasties never matured.

The current emperor attempted to complete the unfinished business of Menelik. His crown prince married the daughter of Seyoum, and he married his daughter to Gugsa, another leader of Tigre, hoping to permanently eliminate the discord between the north and the center through these two marriages. To what extent did he succeed? Since the violent coup in 1916, when the current emperor (Tafari) implicitly became the ruler of Abyssinia, the leaders of Tigre and the central government have often had disagreements, but have never openly rebelled, largely due to the emperor's intelligence. When he was regent, his first act was to restore the governorship of the Tigre province to the descendants of Emperor John, which was their rightful inheritance. However, he feared that the power of the leaders would be too great, endangering the throne. He divided the province into eastern and western parts, so Seyoum governed the western Tigre province, with Adwa as its capital, while his cousin, who was also his deeply hated rival, Gugsa Araya (whose son is now surrendering to the Italian army), became the leader of the eastern Tigre province, stationed in Magale. In the emperor's view, this approach had some effect, because what the emperor feared was that the two would unite and jointly restore the Tigre dynasty. Because they were jealous of each other and divided, they would not pursue this policy. Recently, there was an interesting story in Asmara that can give us a glimpse of their personalities. Because the emperor wanted to reconcile them, he specially ordered them to come to the capital for an audience. Thus, these two cousins had to travel together through Eritrea, where they boarded a ship to Djibouti, and then took a train to the capital. Each had a hundred armed warriors as guards, as well as wives, concubines, key staff, male and female servants, and slaves. The two teams first traveled by car to Asmara, where the Italian consul-general invited them to a banquet to promote unity. The two leaders initially refused to meet, but after repeated persuasion, they agreed to sit at the same table. During the meal, they did not acknowledge each other until near the end of the banquet, when they exchanged a few glasses of champagne and slowly softened. Finally, they shook hands and parted happily. However, this harmony was only superficial. If it had been genuine, Abyssinia's recent history would have been very different from what it is today. When Empress Zewditu abdicated and Tafari became regent, the country was divided into two factions, one supporting the empress and the other supporting the regent. The two cousins (Gugsa and Seyoum) naturally took different sides. As long as one sided with the empress, it would cause the other to conspire with the regent. Conversely, as long as one sided with the regent, it would be enough to cause the other to conspire with the empress.

Because the two were opposed to each other, the major turmoil that occurred at the end of 1929 was able to be overcome smoothly. At that time, the emperor's reform attempts led to a state of unrest, which was only resolved by his efforts to implement the treaty signed with Italy in 1928. The governors of the provinces complained, and the national laws and regulations were non-existent. The leader of the rebellion was Gugsa Wolie, the empress's ex-husband and the leader of central Amhara. The emperor first gave the rebels various opportunities to surrender with honor, but his advice and the empress's advice failed, so he decided to suppress them severely. He gathered the imperial army, commanded by General Mulushi, the Minister of the Army. He also ordered the leaders of the northern provinces to send troops to attack. Among the imperial army, only General Ayana won several battles. The northern provincial leaders all served the emperor and returned victorious, each carrying a large amount of spoils. Among them, Seyoum and Gugsa Araya contributed the most. General Ayana was skilled in strategy and had the help of a French aviator, defeating the rebels and killing their leader. He is currently resisting the Italian army in the north, and military experts consider him the most talented commander in Abyssinia.

Throughout the turmoil, the leaders all appeared to be loyal on the surface, but the attitude of the Tigre leaders, especially Gugsa Araya, was very untrustworthy. He was suspected of secretly inciting the turmoil, and was also despised because of his divorce. His ex-wife was the emperor's beloved niece. Later, he fell ill and died, and his son succeeded him. The emperor was greatly relieved, believing that the son would be easier to control than the father, so he married his daughter to him. Unexpectedly, this son has now surrendered to the Italian army, which shows that the emperor trusted the wrong person. In fact, Gugsa did not have much affection for his father-in-law, and the emperor did not trust him much either. Gugsa disregarded his young wife, allowing her to die of illness, and the emperor harbored resentment in his heart, which he could never forget. When the emperor heard the news that his beloved daughter was seriously ill in distant Tigre, he immediately sent a Greek imperial physician by plane to treat her, but it was too late. The plane later carried the princess's remains back to the capital for burial. This incident proves that the emperor was very dissatisfied with his son-in-law's coldness. Although the emperor still allowed Gugsa to serve as the governor of the eastern Tigre province, he was never at ease in his heart. Therefore, when he issued the general mobilization order, he did not give his son-in-law independent command, but ordered him to be under the control of General Seyoum. Seyoum was Gugsa's own and his father's strong enemy. Gugsa's rebellion and surrender to the Italian army this time was probably due to his resentment of the emperor's suspicion. However, the main motivation was probably to take this opportunity to destroy the Shoa dynasty. Furthermore, Gugsa may have believed that leaning towards Italy was the best way to advance his permanent interests, because if Tigre was under Italian protection, it would certainly need to establish a monarch as a puppet, and anyone who assisted the Italian army would obviously have priority. Whether other leaders will follow Gugsa's rebellion remains to be seen. If he is the only one, then it does not matter much, but if other leaders respond, then it is difficult to say.

U.S. Vice President Garner and Others Passed Through Shanghai Again Yesterday 77

They came ashore for sightseeing and attended a banquet hosted by the American Alumni Association. Some members of the group stayed in Shanghai, while Garner and others returned to their country on the original ship.

U.S. Vice President Garner, Speaker of the House of Representatives Bankhead, a delegation of members of Congress, and representatives of famous newspapers, totaling more than one hundred people, returned home after attending the grand ceremony for the establishment of the independent government of the Philippines. They arrived in Shanghai again on the President Jefferson of the Dollar Steamship Company yesterday afternoon, went sightseeing for half a day, and boarded the original ship that night to leave Shanghai this morning. The details are as follows:

Welcoming Personnel

The ship entered the port at 11:45 a.m. and berthed at Buoys No. 12 and 13 on the Yangshupu river. U.S. Ambassador to China Johnson, along with U.S. Assessor General to China Silkman, U.S. Consul General to Shanghai Cunningham, Marine Corps Commander Beaumont, and representatives of the American community, including the President of the American Chamber of Commerce Franklin, as well as the Director of the Shanghai Office of our Ministry of Foreign Affairs Yu Ming, and Secretary-General Yu Hongjun representing Mayor Wu Tiecheng of this city, boarded the Dollar Company's passenger tender at 11:15 a.m. to welcome them.

Disembarking in Batches

After Garner and others exchanged greetings with the welcoming personnel on the ship, Bankhead and some members of the delegation first boarded the tender and disembarked at the Customs Wharf at 12:30 p.m. They went to the American Club on Fuzhou Road to attend a banquet hosted by the American Alumni Association, with a total of more than 130 guests and hosts in attendance. During the banquet, Senator William King gave a speech, elaborating in detail on the silver issue and the relationship with the Far East. They then went to the Cathay Hotel on the Bund and the U.S. Consulate on Jiangxi Road to rest.

It is reported that a small number of press representatives plan to stay in Shanghai for a longer period of time.

Johnson Returns North

U.S. Ambassador to China Johnson, who has been traveling south since the beginning of the month, previously welcomed Garner and others to Shanghai before they went to the Philippines, then went to Nanjing on official business. He recently came to Shanghai again to welcome Garner and others passing through Shanghai again. As he has been away from Beijing for a long time, the embassy affairs need to be taken care of, and his wife is about to give birth, he has been approved to take the Shanghai-Peiping train with Secretary Salisbury at 4:00 p.m. today, passing through Nanjing without staying, and then going north to return to Peiping.

In order to improve the system, Articles 1 and 3 of the regulations have been amended to increase the number of representatives from the Ministry of Finance to five. In addition to the original representative Xu Kan, four other people will be selected to fill the positions. The amended regulations were announced yesterday, and the amended articles are as follows: Article 1: The Ministry of Finance establishes the Issuing Reserve Management Committee to unify issuance and consolidate the credit of the legal tender. Sub-committees will be established in the commercial port areas as appropriate. Article 3: The Issuing Reserve Management Committee is organized by the following members: (1) Five representatives from the Ministry of Finance; (2) Two representatives each from the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications; (3) Two representatives from the Bankers Association; (4) Two representatives from the Silver and Money Industry Association; (5) Two representatives from the Chamber of Commerce; (6) Five representatives from each issuing bank, designated by the Ministry of Finance.

Ministry of Finance Promulgates Implementation of Measures for Banks Transporting Silver and Applying for Passports 82

Private Smuggling and Carrying Will Be Confiscated and Punished, All Previously Issued Decrees Are Canceled

In order to promote legal tender and strictly prohibit the export of silver, the Ministry of Finance specially formulated measures for transporting silver coins and silver, applying for passports, and punishing private smuggling and carrying. It was officially promulgated on the 24th, and all previously issued decrees were canceled. In addition to ordering the Customs Administration and the Inspector General of Customs to instruct their subordinates to comply, the Ministry yesterday issued separate orders to the National Federation of Commerce and the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce to comply. The Ministry's orders and measures are recorded separately as follows:

Ministry of Finance Instructions to the Two Associations for Compliance

The Ministry of Finance yesterday issued Instruction No. Qianzi 20397, stating: "It has been investigated that the Ministry of Finance has stipulated that from November 4th of this year, the banknotes issued by the Central Bank of China, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications shall be designated as legal tender and cash shall not be used. An order has been issued to comply. Since the promulgation of this order, all decrees repeatedly issued regarding the transportation of silver coins and silver, application for passports, and restrictions on people carrying silver coins and silver, which conflict with the general case of using legal tender, shall be canceled. In addition, six articles of measures for transporting silver coins and silver, applying for passports, and punishing private smuggling and carrying have been formulated to facilitate implementation. In addition to issuing a sub-consultation telegram and circulation, a list of items to be canceled and a copy of the newly formulated measures for transporting silver coins and silver, applying for passports, and punishing private smuggling and carrying are hereby copied and issued for compliance. This order."

Measures for Banks Transporting Silver and Applying for Passports

Article 1: Anyone transporting silver coins or silver shall be transported by the Central Bank of China, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications. The above-mentioned banks transporting silver coins and silver shall hold a passport approved by the Ministry of Finance before they can be transported. Customs checkpoints or military police along the way shall release them based on the Ministry's passport. Article 2: In places where the Central Bank of China, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications have no branches or agencies, silver coins or silver collected by banks, money shops, pawnshops, postal, railway, shipping, and telegraph bureaus, local tax collection agencies, county governments, and other public institutions or public organizations entrusted by them shall be immediately sent to the nearest Central Bank of China, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications, or their agencies, to exchange for legal tender. When transporting, the exchange agencies shall prepare a certificate, stating the number of silver coins or silver and the name of the bank exchanging for legal tender, for inspection by the military police along the way, and notify the nearest bank exchanging for legal tender to facilitate contact. However, when passing through customs checkpoints, they shall be released upon verification of the passport of the Ministry of Finance. Article 3: Anyone purchasing silver materials in accordance with the regulations on the use of silver in silver products shall be given a certificate by the bank selling the silver materials for inspection. However, when passing through customs checkpoints, they shall be released upon verification of the passport of the Ministry of Finance. Article 4: Anyone transporting silver coins or silver privately without applying for a Ministry passport or carrying a certificate from an exchange agency shall be confiscated by military, political, police agencies or customs. The confiscated silver coins and silver shall be confiscated and if it is found that they are deliberately concealed with the intention of smuggling out of the country, the criminals shall be sent to the local court for punishment in accordance with the Provisional Regulations on Punishing Hindrance to National Currency. Article 5: Local people may carry silver coins or silver to the nearest exchange agency to exchange for legal tender within the time limit for exchanging legal tender. Article 6: Except as stipulated in Articles 1, 2, 3, and 5, passengers traveling abroad or to and from the country, and crew members of boats and vehicles, are not allowed to transport or carry silver coins or silver. Violators shall be dealt with separately in accordance with the provisions of Article 4.

List of Items to Be Canceled

(1) Ministry Order No. Qianzi 4501 of April 6, 23rd year: Transportation of silver and other silver that can be used for coinage must have a passport before it can be transported. (2) Ministry Order No. Qianzi 7032 of August 1, 33rd year: Transportation of silver from the inland to Shanghai, Tianjin, and Hankou to the inland must be submitted to the Ministry for approval and a passport issued before it can be transported. (3) Customs Administration Circular No. 210 of November 21, 23rd year: All customs offices must verify the Ministry passport when encountering reports of transporting cash before allowing transportation. Transportation without a passport shall be regarded as smuggling, and the goods shall be confiscated in accordance with regulations. (4) Ministry Order No. Guanzi 10508 of December 12, 23rd year: Regulations stipulate that if the number of silver dollars carried by passengers is found by the military police to be smuggled without a permit and exceeds 1,000 yuan, they shall be detained. (5) Circular No. Qianzi 10858 and Circular No. 1157 of December 26, 23rd year: Regulations stipulate five measures for applying for passports for domestic transportation of cash. (6) Ministry Order No. Guanzi 11235 of January 10, 24th year: Regulations stipulate three measures: the number of silver coins carried by passengers to various parts of the country is limited to 1,000 yuan per person, and passengers going abroad are not allowed to carry national currency. (Order to all customs supervisors) (7) Administration Order No. Guanzi 16010 of March 24th year: Regulations stipulate the number of silver coins allowed to be carried by crew members and sailors. (8) Telegram No. 1320 of May 7, 24th year: Measures of the Beining Railway, transferred by the Ministry of Railways for implementation, to crack down on the smuggling of silver coins and silver out of customs. (9) Provisional measures for the city of Beiping to prohibit the smuggling of cash out of the country, approved by the Ministry in May 24th year. (10) Case approved by the Ministry on May 24th year: The Qingdao Customs Supervisor requested that laborers and poor people going to Dalian from Qingdao be allowed to carry travel expenses within 5 yuan. When questioned by customs officers, they may present them themselves and be ordered to purchase drafts from the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications for release. (11) Case approved by the Ministry on May 25th year: The number of silver coins carried by passengers leaving the country by land from Weihaiwei. (12) Directive No. 14576 of May 28th year to the Inspector General of Customs: Transportation of silver coins without a permit, but without any intention of smuggling abroad, shall be subject to a fine of 20%. (13) Case approved by the Ministry on June 19th year: The Tianjin Customs Supervisor requested that workers exporting from Tianjin who carry cash within 20 yuan and present themselves when questioned by customs officers be ordered to purchase drafts from the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications for release. (Order to the General Affairs Department for transfer and compliance) (14) Ministry Order No. Qianzi 16700 of June 28th year: Regulations stipulate that sailing ships operating at sea are allowed to carry 100 silver coins. If the amount is exceeded without a permit, it shall be confiscated. (15) Reply No. Qianzi 19502 of November 1st year from the Ministry to the Henan Provincial Government: Review and approval of the amended measures to crack down on the smuggling of cash out of the country. (16) Consultation No. Qianzi 15621 of May 16th year from the Ministry to the Hebei Provincial Government: Review and approval of the provisional measures of Hebei Province to prohibit the smuggling of cash out of the country. (17) Ministry telegram of May 21st year to the Mayor of Beiping Yuan: Proposed measures to restrict passengers from carrying cash when leaving the country.

It is proposed to allow a loan of 100,000 yuan, which will be paid by the preparation fund. Is this feasible? Please make a public decision on this case. The resolution was passed. It was decided at the 23rd standing committee meeting that all the 30,000 yuan in cash and ticket funds of the association previously stored in each shop will be used to offset 60% of the cash for bond redemption at the three banks. However, there is still a shortage of 40% in government bond preparation. It is resolved that each shop should prepare on its own and directly redeem from the three banks. It will be implemented after being submitted to the next representative standing committee meeting for decision. (3) It is proposed to design the style of bank drafts, checks, and remittances to comply with the laws and regulations on negotiable instruments. Please review the case. The resolution was passed. (4) On what day will the association's winter management meeting be held? It was decided that it would be held at 2 pm on December 15th. The meeting adjourned at around 3 pm.

New Rice From the Four Rural Areas Floods In, Rice Prices Gradually Become Weak 85

A large amount of new rice from the four rural areas of Wuxi, Changshu, and others has flooded in, and the sales in the interior have become increasingly sluggish. Therefore, rice prices in this city have gradually become weak. Yesterday's selling price of No. 1 white japonica rice was 11.50 to 11 yuan, No. 2 rice was 11 yuan to 10.50 yuan, and other indica and glutinous rice varieties all retreated by 10 cents compared to the previous day. According to people in the rice industry, the listing of new rice would have originally caused a sharp drop in prices, but this year's market prices have remained stable due to the shortening of the exchange rate of legal tender.

According to reports from members Li Futai and Li Jinru, representatives of Shenzhuang, and others from the Fresh Pork Vending Association in this city, the piglets transported from other places to the South Railway Station and purchased from the shanty towns in Nanshi are often intercepted, detained, and arrested by the Ximen Branch along the way when they are rushed to the Xuejiabang Pig Market for sale. Recently, on the 22nd, the Ximen Branch detained Sun Jinyu overnight. For this reason, it sent a letter to the City Chamber of Commerce to transfer to the Public Security Bureau to order all branch offices not to abuse their powers, detain goods, and detain people to maintain human rights. The letter said: Dear Sir/Madam, According to reports from members Li Futai and Li Jinru, representatives of Shenzhuang, and Tang Baoji and Tang Baoquan, representatives of Shenzhuang, and others, the members transported piglets from other places to the Nanshi Railway Station and purchased from the shanty towns in the Nanshi area, and rushed them to the Xuejiabang Pig Market for sale. Before the 20th year of the Republic of China, they used to obtain a permit from the Health Bureau, but it was later abolished and they were allowed to pass freely. However, the jurisdictions of the Ximen Branch still intercept them along the way, and they are not allowed to pass, detaining people and detaining goods, and abusing their powers. For example, on the 13th of this month, Sun Jinyu was entrusted to purchase 18 piglets from the shanty towns in Nanshi and sent them to the Xuejiabang Pig Market for sale on their behalf. When he passed the intersection of Xietu Road and Manufacturing Bureau Road, he was intercepted by the police in charge and detained at the Huixiao Road Police Station, and then released. Unexpectedly, on the evening of the 22nd of this month, the Ximen Branch suddenly raised the old case again, detained Sun Jinyu overnight, and planned to fine him two yuan per pig, totaling 36 yuan. Fortunately, your association negotiated on reasonable grounds and was able to regain his freedom. If this continues, the members will suffer endlessly. Please find a way to provide relief, etc., to the association. It is found that the measures for transporting livestock and obtaining permits have long been revised by the Health Bureau. All healthy livestock transported within the directly administered districts of this city do not need to apply for permits and are allowed to be transported freely. However, those who start from the directly administered district and pass through the concession and are still in the directly administered district (such as from Nanshi to Zhabei) must apply for a special permit and submit it to the municipal government for approval. This was announced on November 20th of the 20th year of the Republic of China. Now, in the same directly administered area of Nanshi, when rushing piglets, the Ximen Branch first detained the goods, obstructing transportation, and then detained Sun Jinyu innocently overnight, hindering the freedom of merchants and violating the spirit of party governance and legislation. Approving the report, I am afraid that the same situation will happen again, so I am specially writing to your association, please transfer it to the Public Security Bureau to order the branch offices not to have the same situation again, in order to maintain the merit and show compassion to merchants. I am extremely grateful.
