Remarks by 何焯贤, Director of the Trademark Bureau, Following the Promulgation of the Revised Trademark Law by Government Order 97

Following the National Government's promulgation of the revised Trademark Law on the 23rd of this month, inquiries were made to Mr. 何焯贤, Director of the Trademark Bureau, regarding the scope of the revisions and future work. Mr. 何 stated that he learned of the government order through newspapers, but as of now, the official document has not yet arrived. This case was resolved with revisions passed on October 31st at the 36th session of the Legislative Yuan. The scope of the revisions was disclosed in the 京中央日报 on October 31st, amending Articles 1, 3, 14, 27, 28, and 40 of the current law, and deleting Article 4. The key points of the revision are as follows: (1) The text used in trademarks, including pronunciation, is included. (2) When two or more persons apply separately for registration of identical or similar trademarks for the same product, registration shall be granted to the person who actually used it first within Chinese territory without interruption. (3) If an approved trademark is used after being altered or having additional marks added to imply something, the Trademark Bureau will, at its discretion or upon the request of an interested party, revoke it. The aforementioned scope of revisions was recorded by the 京中央日报 in its reporting. Whether the scope has been further revised will only be known in detail after the full text of the order arrives. As for the Trademark Bureau's recent work, it involves studying how to revise the Implementing Regulations of the Trademark Law. Because the law has been revised, the Implementing Regulations should also be promptly revised to facilitate the implementation of the new law. However, this must still wait until the full text of the order arrives, after which the proposed revisions to the Implementing Regulations can be submitted to the relevant ministry for adoption and promulgation.

Railway Bureau Revises Sales Method for Regular Tickets; Cancels Original Four-Tiered Fare Reduction; Stipulates Sales Dates for Easier Inspection 104

Based on the resolutions of the Ninth National Railway Transportation Conference, the Ministry of Railways ordered that Article 1 of the Regulations for the Issuance of Regular Train Tickets be revised to state that regular train tickets are sold by the Traffic Department of each Railway Bureau, and that sales methods be properly discussed. The Traffic Department of the Railway Bureau believes that the original method used by the railway has been in place for a long time and is no longer fully suitable for the current situation. Furthermore, the old method of dividing the fares into four tiers based on distance, with excessively large differences in the discount rates between each tier, often resulted in lower fares for longer distances than for shorter distances, which was also inappropriate. Moreover, sales at any time made inspection inconvenient, and there were doubts about whether passengers were using expired tickets fraudulently. In order to remedy the above shortcomings, the method has been revised as follows: (1) The original four-tiered fare reduction method has been canceled to ensure fairness, with higher fares for longer distances. (2) The discount rate method has been revised to charge the price of 40 one-way tickets for a one-month period, the price of 110 one-way tickets for a three-month period, the price of 190 one-way tickets for a six-month period, and the price of 340 one-way tickets for a twelve-month period. (3) The sales date is limited to the first day of each month. If sold after the first day, the validity period is also limited to the end of the month to prevent expired tickets from being used fraudulently. A monthly stamp will be added to the regular ticket to facilitate inspection by ticket inspectors and collectors. The above method has been approved by the Railway Bureau for trial implementation and has been reported to the Ministry of Railways for record.

Robbery at the Dai Family Residence in Gaoqiao Town 106

戴彰达, a farmer living in house number eight of the Dai family residence in Gaoqiao Town, Pudong, made a living from farming and was fairly well-off. The night before last, around midnight, four or five robbers suddenly came, all speaking the local dialect and wearing short blue and green cloth shirts and trousers. They jumped into the house through the window. One robber brandished a sharp pointed knife, threatening the victims not to make a sound. They then began to ransack the house, overturning chests and cabinets. A total of more than ten yuan in foreign banknotes were stolen, but the clothes were left behind. Later, seeing that Dai's wife was wearing a pair of gold earrings, they forced her to take them off. Dai refused and argued with the robbers, causing him to be injured in the waist and back. In the end, the robbers stole the earrings and fled with their loot. Afterwards, the incident was reported to the local police station for investigation.

Violent Brawl Between Two Gangs of Workers at the Dafeng Cotton Mill; Hu Zhongyuan, Unfamiliar with Swimming, Drowns 107

At the Dafeng Cotton Mill in 潭子口, Zhabei, on the Suzhou Creek, two gangs of workers from Jiangbei (north of the Yangtze River) and Hubei (a province) clashed with each other over business yesterday morning around 11 o'clock at the mill gate. The Jiangbei gang gathered over a hundred people, with a larger presence, while the Hubei gang had only a few people. As a result of the brawl, the Hubei gang was outnumbered, and five people, including 余江生, 徐华五, 吴黄高, and 吴耀银, jumped into the Suzhou Creek to swim away. 徐华五, 吴黄高, and 吴耀银 managed to climb onto a boat and escape. 余江生 swam to the opposite bank and was taken to the 普陀路 police station by a Chinese detective from the British Concession, number 1159, for questioning. 胡忠元 drowned and his body sank to the bottom of the river. The body had not been recovered by the evening. The local police station detained more than thirty workers from the Jiangbei gang and took them to the station for investigation. The Customs Water Police Station dispatched detective 顾文奎 after the incident to investigate the scene and assist in recovering the body.

Major Drug Case Cracked at South Railway Station; Public Security Bureau Takes Custody of Ye Zicai; Ye Firmly Denies Smuggling Drugs and Is Willing to Face Extreme Punishment; Special Second Court Rules to Temporarily Not Transfer Him and Continue the Investigation 109

At around 5:00 PM on the 23rd, 王长根, a native of Jianqiao, Hangzhou, transported six white cloth flour sacks filled with goods by handcart to the cargo depot at the rear gate of the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway South Station in the Nanshi district, entrusting the Xie Daxing Transport Company there to transport them to Lanxi, Zhejiang. Because the company asked Wang for a letter of authorization from the consignor and inquired about the name and quantity of the goods inside, Wang only stated that the sacks contained medicinal materials and could not answer any other questions, which aroused suspicion. The company sent an employee to accompany Wang back to retrieve the letter. Wang tried to escape halfway, but the employee apprehended him and handed him over to the patrol police, who took him to the Ximen Public Security Branch. The branch sent a detective to take Wang to the South Station, where the Xie Daxing Transport Company reported the incident to the South Station Police Section. The inspector opened the sacks for inspection and discovered that they contained raw materials for the manufacture of red pills, such as heroin and morphine, worth more than 100,000 yuan. A related person, 胡世木, was subsequently apprehended at the rear gate of the station. According to Hu, he was instructed by 台州 native 叶子才, who lived at No. 21, Ren Shou Lane, Wang Zhi Road in the French Concession, to instruct 王长根 to transport the goods to the station for loading. The Ximen Public Security Branch's Detective Division Chief, 沈交达, dispatched detectives to accompany 王 and 胡 to the French Concession police station to request the dispatch of detectives to Ye Zicai's residence to arrest him. Ye was taken back to the police station for detention and further investigation. This has been reported in yesterday's newspaper. At 2:30 PM yesterday afternoon, the French Concession police handed over 叶子才 to the Criminal Division One of the Special Second Court. Judge 熊汇苹 questioned him. Lawyer 姚肇第 of the Police Department stated the case, saying that the Police Department, according to the Public Security Bureau's report that the defendant was involved in drug trafficking, arrested the defendant. Since the Police Department still needs to conduct a detailed investigation, please postpone the hearing. Shanghai Public Security Bureau commissioned legal counsel 詹纪凤 and detectives to arrive at the court. Lawyer Zhan stated the process of uncovering the drugs to the court and requested permission to transfer the defendant to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation. The defendant 叶子才 denied handing the drugs over to 胡 and 王, claiming that it was a malicious accusation and requested the court to conduct a detailed investigation. If it is verified, he is willing to accept extreme punishment. He also hired lawyer 葛之覃 to defend him, stating that the defendant is the owner of the Jinghua Woolen Mill and is a legitimate businessman. He submitted nine books of the Jinghua Mill's accounts as evidence. Next, the representative of the Public Security Bureau, lawyer Zhan, stated that the Public Security Bureau is now bringing 王长根 and 胡世木 to the court and requested to question them. The court ordered the two witnesses, 王 and 胡, to be brought to the court. First, Wang Changgen testified that he lived in Jianqiao, Hangzhou, and came to Shanghai on the 21st due to a disagreement with his parents. He went to the home of his relative 胡世木. On the morning of the 23rd, around 11:00 AM, a friend of Hu Shimu sent six sacks to Hu's place and entrusted Hu to send them to the station. Because Hu had to go out to do business, he asked me to transport them instead. At the transportation company, Hu said that the friend said that the items were contraband, but the friend said it was okay, so I transported them on his behalf. I don't know the name of Hu's friend, but I would recognize him if I saw him. The officer then pointed to the defendant and asked Wang if this was the person. Wang looked back at the defendant's face and replied yes, this is the person. Ye, hearing Wang's testimony, said to Wang, "You have to speak with your conscience." Then, 胡世木 arrived at the court and testified that he lived on Rue du Père Huc and usually sold small pieces of cloth. Wang Changgen is a relative of his. His cousin married Wang. On the morning of the 23rd, around 11:00 AM, Ye sent the sacks to my house and entrusted me to send them to the transportation company. Because I had to go out to do business and didn't have time, I asked Wang to transport them instead. The officer asked Hu, "How did Ye transport the sacks to your house?" Hu replied, "I was upstairs at the time and didn't see how Ye transported them, but he came upstairs alone, and that's when I knew." The defendant 叶子方 then testified that he went to the shipping company on the afternoon of the 23rd and went to the home of his friend 滕仲高 at No. 35, Xihu Lane, Ximen Road, at 11:00 AM, requesting an investigation. At this point, the officer said that the Police Department still needs to investigate the evidence in this case. The defendant will be detained temporarily, and he cannot be transferred today. The hearing will be continued at 2:00 PM on the 29th. The defendant was taken back into custody, and 王长根 and 胡世木 were taken back by the officials from the Public Security Bureau.

A Major Transformation in the Buddhist Community; Sending Monks Abroad to Study; The Siam Study Group Organized First; The Ceylon Dharma Study Group Followed 110

Buddhist believers in Shanghai, such as 释悲观, 性敎, etc., organized the Siam Study Group to promote Chinese culture and study Siamese Buddhism, with the support of Masters such as 太虚 and 圆瑛. They are scheduled to go abroad soon. At the same time, the Chinese Buddhist Association will also send several young Buddhist disciples to islands such as India and Ceylon to study Southern Buddhism. The Datong News Agency reported the above measures by the Buddhist community, transforming from passive self-cultivation to active progress, and the news is recorded below.

Siam Study Group

The Siam Study Group, initiated by 释悲观, 性敎, etc., is currently preparing in Beijing, as they are about to go abroad. They are scheduled to come to Shanghai at the end of the month to meet with Master 太虚 to discuss matters related to going abroad. At the same time, the group received a letter of support from Mr. 叶恭绰, who specifically contributed 100 yuan for travel expenses. The original letter from Mr. Ye reads: "I have learned that I am presenting 100 yuan in legal currency to help with travel expenses. I hope you will take care of yourselves for the sake of Dharma. I look forward to it. Respectfully, 叶恭绰 to Masters 释悲观, 性敎, etc."

Ceylon Dharma Study Group

The Shanghai Buddhist Pure Land Society, in order to connect Chinese and Indian Buddhism, proposed to the Chinese Buddhist Association to send several young Buddhist disciples to the island of Ceylon to study the Sangha Vinaya and Southern Buddhism. It is now known that the Chinese Buddhist Association has adopted the proposal and organized the Ceylon Dharma Study Group. Those who have registered include 慧松, 法周, 惟幼, 惟实, 惟植, 隆安, 林慧白, etc., seven people. They are now at the Pure Land Society, waiting for a letter from Master Narada, a Ceylonese monk who has come to Shanghai to preach, to set a date for departure. The departure date is expected to be at the end of January next year.

Health Bureau Calls Fecal Merchants to Discuss Building Fecal Storage Ponds 111

The Shanghai Health Bureau, noting that fecal merchants in Shanghai are unable to sell human waste because rural areas are switching to using chemical fertilizers, resulting in a lack of buyers and no place to store or pile the waste, convened a meeting yesterday morning at 10:00 AM in the bureau's business office, gathering all fecal merchants in Shanghai and representatives from the Public Security, Finance, and other bureaus to discuss solutions. The meeting was chaired by Mr. 江世澄, director of the Health Bureau's Second Division. After mutual discussion, it was decided to still assist the fecal merchant 马鸿记 in preparing large fecal vessels to transport the waste, and to have the sanitation engineer design and build fecal storage ponds to store the waste.

New Zha Branch Bureau: Confession Obtained from Thief Ji Xiang, Hatched Robbery of Panjiawan by Chou San, Each Person's Confession Partially Corroborates and Partially Denies 112

The Anti-Crime Squad of the Municipal Police Bureau's New Zha Branch Bureau, led by Deputy Squad Leader Bao Ziying and Shi Zuhan, received a confidential tip from an informant named Jin Kang around 2:00 AM the day before yesterday (Friday), indicating that a gang of thieves was hiding in Yongxiang Lane, Datong Road, and other locations. The Squad Leader immediately reported to Branch Bureau Chief Liao, who dispatched patrol officers Wu Dichen and Chi Baoren, along with Anti-Crime Squad Deputy Foreman Li Guiqing, to apprehend eleven suspected thieves. This was previously reported in the newspaper. It has since been learned that a female suspect, Zhu Shenshi, was apprehended that very night, and the following day a person named Yu Jin, suspected of buying stolen goods, was also brought in for questioning, bringing the total to thirteen. Their testimonies are as follows:

Ding Yaozhang testified: 32 years old, from Yangzhou, residing at No. 30, Yongxiang Lane, Datong Road. A few nights ago, Chou San gave me a pistol. I handed it over to Pan Er, who, along with Wang Xiaoliuzi, Li Baolong, and Pan Er Xiaokai, went to Panjiawan to rob people. They stole fur coats, overcoats, cotton robes, and other items, which Chou San later pawned. The robbery was Chou San's idea. I received two yuan as my share. About three or four months ago, five or six people robbed a household on the boundary road in Hongkou, attacking a rickshaw puller. I received 2,000 copper coins as my share. The confiscated pistol was entrusted to me by Chou San to keep, in preparation for future crimes.

Dai Baolong testified: 30 years old, from Funing, residing in a shack on Qimei Road, Hongkou. This month, along with Wang Xiaoliuzi, Ding Yaozhang, and others, I robbed the Panjiawan area, obtaining similar loot. I received two yuan as my share. We also robbed a place on the boundary road in Hongkou, receiving 2,000 copper coins, and robbed a houseboat on Qimei Road, Hongkou, receiving two or three yuan. We were also planning to rob a rice shop in Zhoujia Lane, Hongkou, and a place on Changan Road, as well as rob an old man of the banknotes in his cloth bag, but these attempts were unsuccessful. (The Anti-Crime Squad investigated and summoned the old man, Jin Rongkang, who testified that he was carrying banknotes worth tens of thousands of yuan in his cloth bag and was taking them to the New Zha branch of the Bank of China when several bandits attempted to rob him near Da Wang Temple, but failed.)

Wang Xiaoliuzi testified: 42 years old, from Yancheng, residing at No. 21, Sande Lane, Tanziwan. I previously worked at a cloth factory behind the nunnery north of the railway, where I committed a crime, obtaining twenty-one bolts of cloth and other items such as electric fans, which I sold through a person named Wang Songlin. On the 14th of this month, along with Ding Yaozhang, Dai Baolong, Chou San, Pan San Xiaokai, Pan Er, and others, I robbed Panjiawan, receiving two yuan as my share. We were planning to rob other places in Hongkou, but were unsuccessful. The pistol found on me belongs to Pan San Xiaokai.

Zhang Lianghe testified: 27 years old, from Funing, residing at Jingyuan Tou, Gaochang Temple, Nanshi. I previously served eight years in prison in the French Concession, so I changed my name to Jiang Dehe. I was released from prison in June of this year. Chou San, Dai Baolong, Xiao Erzi (i.e., Zhang Xiaoliuzi) and others asked me to rob a place near the Bao Weituan (i.e., Panjiawan). At that time, Dai Baolong gave me a pistol.

Zhang Xiaosi testified: 22-23 years old, from Yancheng, residing in a shack by the railway on Zhaozhou Road, Nanshi. The stolen goods from the crimes he committed came from the Hugunying, Guohuo Road, and other places. I have never been to Zhabei. Because they arrested him, they also arrested me.

Hong Dengyun testified: 19 years old, from Yancheng, residing at the Huayang Bathhouse, Hengfeng Road. I came to Shanghai from Zhangshan Bridge in the countryside because Zhang Xiaoliuzi's older brother asked me to deliver a letter to him, telling him to go back to work. I stayed overnight at his house that night and was unexpectedly arrested along with him.

Du Longxing testified: 24 years old, from Funing, residing in a shack in Panjiawan. I work at the Public Works Bureau. Wang Xiaoliuzi is my neighbor, and he knows that I have been in trouble with the law. He suspects that I inform on him, so he bears a grudge and accused me of being an accomplice.

Lushangzhong testified: 30 years old, from Han Ning, residing in Huazibang, making a living by pulling a rickshaw. Du Longxing accused me of informing on him, so I was arrested along with him.

He and Wang Youshan said they wanted to manage the theater and, if successful, would hire me as a staff member. Therefore, I am temporarily staying at a friend's house in Le'an Lane. I know someone surnamed Dai, but I don't know what they do.

Later, they asked me to take it away. They are all friends of my husband, so I know them.

Wang Songlin testified: 35 years old, from Haimen, residing in a shack at the Huzhou Guild Hall, Huiwen Road. I used to work with Wang Xiaoliuzi in the same factory and know him. In September, he asked me to sell Patriotic Twill on his behalf. I don't know where it came from.

Further Trial of Ancient Vase Case, Cheng Linsheng Surrendered Himself Yesterday, Content of Mortgage Dispute Complex 115

Chi Yunfei, from Fujian, accused Jiang Yuting, the owner of Yuanzhang Jewelry Store at No. 99, Shanxi Road, from Wuxi, in the First Special District Court of defrauding him of an ancient Yuexuan vase worth tens of thousands of yuan. The court has repeatedly heard the case, and the details have been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Ye Shengchao held another hearing in the Fifth Criminal Court, and witnesses Yang Jingbing and Cheng Linsheng both appeared in court. Yang testified first, stating that on a certain day in August, because his wife was ill, he went to the home of his relative, Ye Chengming. Chi Yunfei happened to be there and said that the ancient vase had been defrauded by Jiang Yuting and that he planned to sue. Because both parties were friends, I acted as a mediator. I went with Chi to Jiang's place, and Jiang said that he had obtained the vase with great difficulty, so how could he easily let it go? He would only return the vase to Chi if I assumed responsibility for 6,000 yuan, because Cheng Linsheng owed him money. After three mediation attempts, we could not reach a resolution. Then, Cheng Linsheng testified that after mortgaging the vase to Yang Run Shen last year, it was transferred to Chi. In August, Jiang Yuting came and said that the daughter of a Tai Pan from an English-American Tobacco Company wanted to buy the vase, so I informed Chi Yunfei and asked him to bring the vase. Jiang said that he needed to take it for a day or two and would return it. Chi did not trust him, but because I had frequent transactions with Jiang, I did not suspect anything and issued a guarantee on his behalf. Chi then handed the vase to Jiang. Who knew it was a deception? The court then asked, according to the defendant's testimony, did you mortgage two diamond rings and this vase to him for a debt of 18,000 yuan? Cheng replied that there was no such thing. When Jiang took the two rings, he also said that someone wanted to buy them. I did not know that it was a deceitful trick. I also intend to accuse Jiang. The defendant claimed that Cheng had mortgaged the vase to him and that the vase had been given to him once in April. He asked that Pan Mingxun, a comprador from the Public Works Department, be summoned as a witness. The court ordered that the hearing be postponed for one week.

County Citizens Hold the 7th Plowing Cattle Competition 116

405 Head of Plowing Cattle Participated, An Unprecedented Grand Occasion, Wansheng Farm Awarded Overall First Place in the Judging Result

The Zhuanqiao Public Education Hall in Shanghai County held the 7th Plowing Cattle Competition yesterday. Four hundred and five head of plowing cattle participated, and over one thousand representatives from various circles and citizens attended, creating an unprecedented grand occasion. As a result of the judging, Wansheng Farm was awarded overall first place, and the awards are scheduled to be given on the 30th of this month. The details are recorded as follows:

A Glimpse of the Venue The reception area was located in the Chongnong Hall, and the registration area was located at Nongjiao Road and Xuezhi Road. The cattle field was equipped with a waiting field. Those bringing cattle to the event went to the registration office to register, collect their competition certificate and food certificate, and attach a numbered tag to the cattle's body. The cattle competing were categorized into groups based on age, excluding bulls, including water buffalo and yellow cattle: Leading Calf, Two-Tooth, Four-Tooth, Six-Tooth, Full-Mouth, and other categories. After the cattle participating in the competition were numbered and tagged, they were tied in the designated locations, waiting for the judges to inspect them. After the inspection was completed, the cattle were not allowed to be led out of the field without permission. The conformation was inspected in the morning, and the physical strength was inspected in the afternoon. Sick cattle were treated by veterinarians, and excellent cattle were photographed.

Attending Representatives Included Cai Wuji, representative of the Ministry of Industry; Wu Huanru from the Social Affairs Bureau; Yang Huiming from the County Education Bureau; Zhang Yi from the County Public Education Hall; Wang Zhaolin, Chen Shunyun, Cheng Shaohui, Wu Deming, Shen Jiucheng, Pan Weiyuan, Zhao Songlin, He Ruitang, Zhang Daqing, Zhao Wu, Wu Genglai, Shen Baixian, Yu Quansheng, Gu Tuxiang, Tang Yinxian, Yan Qiugen, Zhao Ronghua, Liu Yaoshan, Wu Jinsai, Chen Changgen, Zhang Shichang, and over two thousand other people from all walks of life. The cattle that arrived included fifty Full-Mouth cattle, sixty-eight Six-Tooth cattle, fifty-five Four-Tooth cattle, sixty-five Two-Tooth cattle, and seventy-seven Leading Calf cattle.

Judging Meeting At 9:00 AM, the judging meeting was held. Chairman was Cai Wuji. The discussion resulted in the following: (1) In addition to reviewing the conformation this year, the physical strength will also be inspected. (2) The top two in each group for conformation inspection will be subjected to physical strength inspection. (3) For the scoring method, the average of the conformation and physical strength scores will be calculated. (4) Four-Tooth cattle will plow one-quarter of a mu of field, and Six-Tooth and older cattle will plow half a mu. (5) The depth of plowing is stipulated to be two cun, and artificial methods of driving the cattle are not allowed. (6) Standards: Speed, Uniformity, Straightness, and Respiratory Condition. Ten rows per plot. (7) Scoring standards: Speed 30 points, Uniformity 30 points, Straightness 20 points, Respiratory Condition 20 points. (8) When selecting the overall average first, second, and third place, conformation will be the standard, and physical strength will not be considered. (9) Any cattle that have received awards in the past that are still able to win awards this year will be listed in the prize list. (10) The judging will be held in two stages: preliminary and final.

Group Review A decision was made to conduct group reviews: Conformation Review, Full-Mouth Cattle Group: Cheng Shaohui, Cai Wuji, Wu Deming, Wu Gengrong; Six-Tooth Cattle Group: Zhang Jixian, He Zhengli; Four-Tooth Cattle Group: Zhao Wu, Pan Weiyuan; Two-Tooth Cattle Group: Yang Xingye, Gao Depei; Leading Calf Cattle Group: Zhu Xianbin, Yang Huiming; Other Cattle Group: Shen Jiucheng, Zhang Huangxi. Physical Strength Review, Full-Mouth Cattle Group: Six farmers, Cai Wuji, Cheng Shaohui; Six-Tooth Cattle Group: Zhao Wu, Pan Weiyuan, Wu Gengrong; Four-Tooth Cattle Group: Shen Jiucheng.

Review Results Overall First Place: Wansheng Farm, Second Place: Song Xin, Third Place: Wang Xigen. Leading Calf Group First Place: Wang Shengrong, Second Place: Wang Liutang, Third Place: Zhu Quanzhong, Excellent: Wang Zhixue, Yu Yousong; Two-Tooth Group First Place: Chi Xishan, Second Place: Xu Jinchang, Third Place: Liu Yongtian, Excellent: Chen Changgeng; Four-Tooth Group First Place: Wang Xigen, Second Place: Lu Kongran, Third Place: Zhao Caigen; Six-Tooth Group First Place: Song Xinchun, Second Place: Zhuang Xiaodi, Third Place: He Chunhua; Full-Mouth Group First Place: Wansheng Farm, Second Place: Zhu Rusheng, Third Place: Du Wenbin, Excellent: Cao Jinsheng, Zhu Xifeng, Bao Yongtang, Shen Menglian, Yan Xiaobao, Liu Shengxiang, Gu Ersheng.

Husbandry Guidance At 3:30 PM, husbandry knowledge guidance was conducted. Cai Wuji, Cheng Shaohui, and others provided sincere guidance. On the same day, the Ministry of Industry's Animal Disease Prevention and Control Office held a plowing cattle protection exhibition at the Chongnong Institute, displaying over a hundred items. It is reported that the hall is scheduled to award prizes on the 30th of this month.

Brutal and Ferocious, Horrifying to Hear, A Tragic Incident of a Mother Beating Her Own Daughter to Death, The Girl's Urine and Feces Stained Her Clothes and She Was Often Severely Beaten, Recently She Was Severely Injured and Died From Being Struck With Firewood 117

Jiang Ahzhong from Wuxi is employed as a gatekeeper at the No. 5 Shenxin Cotton Mill. His wife, Wang, is 22 years old and has given birth to two daughters. The elder daughter, Rongdi, who is only three years old, is fostered in their hometown. The younger daughter is still in swaddling clothes and is personally cared for by Wang. On the 27th of last month, Jiang moved to the three-story attic of Yang Mao's house at No. 36, Jifu Lane, Qiqihar Road, Yangshupu. On the 5th of this month, his elder daughter Rongdi, who was being fostered in Wuxi, was also sent back. The girl was naturally prone to crying and had only just begun to babble. She could not control her urination and defecation. Her mother, Wang,

was very violent, and did not know how to guide children. Whenever she saw the child crying, she would beat her. If she encountered urine and feces staining the child's clothes, she would roar incessantly and severely scold her. She was especially cruel to Rongdi and had no "慈母慈母(cimǔ)" attitude at all. Although the ignorant child was repeatedly severely beaten, she still urinated and defecated, and cried even more. Yang Mao, the second landlord, could not bear to watch. At first, she thought that Wang was young and unskilled in raising children, so she gave her special guidance. Unexpectedly, Wang not only ignored her, but also

went from bad to worse. She regarded Rongdi as a horse or cow. To avoid being implicated in the future, she issued an eviction order, asking Jiang to move. Jiang, however, was reluctant to leave, so he still lived there. Unexpectedly, Wang's treatment of Rongdi became even more vicious. The day before yesterday, the girl happened to defecate in her pants again. Wang then took a piece of firewood and violently struck her head, creating a hole, and blood flowed straight out. She not only did not feel any pity, but also took off the pants that the child was wearing, which were stained with feces, and covered the child's head and face with them.

She also used rope

to tightly tie one part of the pants around the child's neck. In addition, the child's hands and feet were all tied with rope. The child's weak life was subjected to this severe torment, so there was no hope of survival. Therefore, before the end of the day, the child was tortured to death. After the child died, Wang showed no grief. She wrapped the body in a large sheet and placed it in the bedroom, intending to find an opportunity to dispose of it. Later, Yang Mao was hanging clothes on the terrace and passed by the door of the room. She saw a bundle in the room and became suspicious. Upon inspection, the matter was revealed. In a short time, the news spread throughout the neighborhood, and the neighbors were all outraged by the woman's

cruel and vicious nature. Although the victim was her own daughter, the case involved a human life and could not be concealed. While people were discussing this, the Yulin Road Police Station, acting on a confidential report, sent Detective Huang Yufu to the scene to investigate together with a foreign detective. Yang Mao and others described the incident in detail. At this time, the woman was still trying to escape, but was arrested. The child's body was taken to the morgue on Fellen Road for examination. Yesterday morning, the case was reported to the Prosecutor's Office of the First Special District Local Court. Prosecutor Guo Wei, accompanied by two forensic doctors, Wei and Zhang, and clerk Wang Zuyi, arrived at the morgue and confirmed that the girl, Jiang Rongdi,

was covered in injuries, with the injuries to the head and buttocks being the most severe. It was determined that she had died from serious injuries caused by being beaten while alive. Under questioning of Jiang Wang and various witnesses, the court determined that Jiang Wang was suspected of committing a crime and ordered her temporary detention. The Police Station was instructed to prosecute and await trial by the court. The child's body was sent to the Zhenru Forensic Medicine Research Institute for dissection at the request of the forensic doctor for medical research. Prosecutor Guo approved this and instructed the institute to hand over the body to Pushan Villa for burial after the dissection. This kind of tragic incident of a mother beating her own children to death is rare in Shanghai.

Yisheng Silk and Satin Foreign Goods Store Stole Hundreds of Thousands in National Taxes, Sea Customs Anti-Smuggling Section Dispatched Personnel to Investigate and Crack the Case, Still a Large Amount of Untaxed Goods Being Sought 118

Yisheng Silk and Satin Foreign Goods Store, located at No. 54, Jixian Lane, Nanjing Road, was founded by Liu Mingjia, a wealthy merchant from Huzhou. It has been in business for over ten years. Liu initially started by dealing in piece goods of silk and wool fabrics. Most of the Western silk and wool fabrics sold by major silk and satin stores in Shanghai were retailed from Yisheng, allowing Liu to sit back and reap the profits. In less than ten years, he became a wealthy man. Recently, the Anti-Smuggling Section of the Jianghai Customs suddenly received a confidential report stating that most of the goods imported by Yisheng over the years had been smuggled, or that the quantity had been underreported. Over the past ten years, the amount of unpaid taxes was considerable. Upon receiving the report, the section, recognizing the seriousness of the case, secretly instructed its officers to exert several weeks of effort. They confirmed that the store had indeed committed the aforementioned acts. Yesterday, they urgently applied to the First Special District Court for a search warrant and, together with detectives from the Central Police Station, rushed to the store at No. 54, Jixian Lane, Nanjing Road at 3:30 PM to search it. The search lasted for two hours. As a result, all the accounts and a large amount of unsold untaxed goods, worth hundreds of thousands of yuan, were seized. In addition to sealing up the goods, the accounts and other items were immediately taken away, and several key personnel from the store were detained and temporarily held at the Police Station, awaiting transfer to the court for questioning. It is reported that the Anti-Smuggling Section is particularly concerned about a recent large-scale import of untaxed goods, especially silk and wool piece goods, which has had a significant impact on national tax revenue. Therefore, the investigation is being carried out with extreme diligence, hoping to crack the case in the shortest possible time in order to deter criminals and emphasize the importance of taxation.

After Xia Housheng's Death, His Concubine Sues on Behalf of Her Son, Sues Principal Wife to Confirm Biological Son 119

Xia Housheng, a local resident and owner of Shunyu Rice Store at No. 20, Remi Road, French Concession, lived in the store with his wife, Xia Li (41 years old this year), son, Shan Zhang (15 years old), and daughter, Xiuzhi (11 years old). In August 1933, he took Zhu (23 years old), a local young woman, as a concubine and rented a house for her at No. 8, Xinxingshun Lane, Gansidong Road, where they lived together. Unfortunately, Xia Housheng died of illness on October 26 of last year. On June 20 of this year, Xia's concubine Zhu gave birth to a posthumous son, named Baobao. Because the mother and son were not tolerated by the principal wife, Xia Zhu, in her capacity as the legal representative, along with her son Baobao, hired a lawyer and filed a lawsuit in the Civil Court of the Second Special District against Xia Li, Xia Shanzhang, and Xia Xiuzhi, the mother, son, and daughter, seeking a division of Xia Housheng's estate. During the initial trial, the plaintiff Xia Zhu presented Qian, the second landlord, to the court to testify that Xia Housheng had lived with Xia Zhu during his lifetime. As a result, the court ruled that Xia Baobao should receive a proportionate share of Xia Housheng's estate with Xia Shanzhang and Xia Xiuzhi, while the part of the lawsuit concerning Xia Zhu was dismissed. The defendant, Xia Li, appealed to the Third Branch of the High Court, but the court ruled to change the original verdict and dismissed the appellant's original lawsuit, as the appellee Xia Baobao had not had his identity confirmed. Now, Xia Zhu, again in her capacity as the legal representative, using her son's real name Xia Baobao, hired lawyers Wang Heng and Gu to file a lawsuit in the court of the Second Special District against Xia Li, Xia Shanzhang, Xia Xiuzhi, and others, seeking confirmation of the illegitimate son. Yesterday, Judge Tu Shenjie held a hearing in the Sixth Civil Court. The plaintiff, Xia Baobao's legal representative Xia Zhu, and her lawyer appeared in court. First, the lawyer representing the plaintiff stated the grounds for the lawsuit and the object of the requested ruling. The defendants' lawyer, Lu Congzu, appeared in court and presented three points of defense, stating that the defendants did not know that the plaintiff was born to Xia Zhu, nor did they know that Xia Housheng had taken Xia Zhu as a concubine during his lifetime. Regarding the legal points, they had already been determined in the previous judgment on estate division, and they requested that the plaintiff's lawsuit be dismissed. The court questioned Xia Zhu, the plaintiff's mother, about her cohabitation with Xia Housheng during his lifetime and the circumstances of the birth of her son. After the judge concluded the questioning, he announced the adjournment and scheduled the verdict for the 30th of this month.

Peng Taiyi of Sichuan has long been renowned for his writing and moral character. After decades of effort, he wrote "Textual Research on Laoism," totaling five volumes with nine chapters, further divided into 115 sub-items; "Textual Research on Buddhism," totaling six volumes with fifteen chapters, further divided into 66 sub-items; "Textual Research on Confucianism," totaling seven volumes with seventeen chapters, further divided into 119 sub-items; "Textual Research on Judaism," totaling four volumes with eight chapters, further divided into 36 sub-items; "Textual Research on Christianity," totaling seven volumes with fifteen chapters, further divided into 117 sub-items; "Textual Research on Islam," totaling six volumes with eleven chapters, further divided into 76 sub-items; "Textual Research on Various Minor Religions," and four types of philosophy; and "Conclusion on New Religions," totaling six volumes with twenty chapters, among other books. These are now being published by the Shanghai Society for Religious and Philosophical Research. The summarized pre-order regulations are listed below: (1) The "World Religious Great Harmony Complete Works" contains approximately 700,000 words, using 45-pound newsprint and typesetting in No. 3 font. The book format is 6 inches wide and 8.5 inches long. The total number of pages is approximately 1,000. Each part will be bound into ten paperbound volumes. (2) The pre-order period for this book is from November 5th, 1935 to December 5th, 1935. (3) During the pre-order period, the price for each set is 3 yuan in silver dollars for mail orders. Those who order after the deadline will be charged the list price of 4 yuan in silver dollars. (4) The publication date of this book is approximately in March 1936. (5) Packing and postage are charged separately. (6) Correspondence address: Society for Religious and Philosophical Research, No. 532 Baker Road, Shanghai.

Notice from the Two Roads Bureau: Regulations for Joint Transportation of Dangerous Goods, etc. 134

The Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration issued a notice yesterday stating that, with the exception of dangerous goods, explosives, live poultry and livestock, coffins, etc., less-than-carload freight for which the shipper is responsible, joint transportation was previously approved in consultation with the Tianjin-Pukou Railway. In order to facilitate shippers, the Tianjin-Pukou Railway has again approved that dangerous goods for which the freight can be calculated from a minimum of 50 kilograms according to the Ministry of Railways regulations are also permitted to be handled with joint transportation. The regulations are as follows: (1) These dangerous goods may be loaded using empty return vehicles and are not limited to loading only the minimum quantity per vehicle, so that they can be transported as soon as they arrive. (2) Vehicles transporting these dangerous goods from the Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway can be reloaded into the shipper-responsible less-than-carload vehicles of the Tianjin-Pukou Railway after crossing the track at Pukou. However, special care must be taken during loading and unloading to avoid danger and must be separated from other goods to ensure safety. (3) These dangerous goods must be securely packaged in strict accordance with the methods prescribed by the Ministry of Railways and must be affixed with dangerous goods labels; otherwise, they will not be accepted for transport. (4) The railway will be responsible for guarding the transportation of these dangerous goods, and no escort is required. All handover and transit procedures will be handled in accordance with the responsible cargo regulations, but the railway will not be liable for any losses. The above regulations will be implemented from December 1st. Furthermore, there is already joint transportation of coffins in practice, which the Tianjin-Pukou Railway has agreed to continue.

Huikang Steamer Hits Reef in Quanzhou: Forward Hold Flooded, Now Aground North of Dazhui Island—Urgent Discussions to Rescue 135

The Huikang Steamer, belonging to the Shanghai Branch of the Huitong Steamship Company, hit a reef in Quanzhou on its way to Xiamen. The forward hold is flooded. There are ongoing discussions to send a ship to rescue it. The details are as follows:

Reef Impact in Quanzhou. The Huikang Steamer, belonging to Huitong Steamship Company, located at No. 44 Guangdong Road, Shanghai, has been sailing to various coastal ports without a fixed route. This time, it was fully loaded with soybean cakes, soybeans, and other items from Yingkou and Yantai to be unloaded at various ports in South China. The ship first arrived in Quanzhou, Fujian. On the 23rd of this month, it unloaded all cargo in Quanzhou. At that time, 430 tons of cargo for Xiamen were still left in the hold, which was to be transported by the ship. On the 23rd, after departing from Quanzhou and sailing to the vicinity of Dazhui Island at the port, at approximately 5:00 AM, due to fog, the ship mistakenly struck a submerged reef.

Two Holds Flooded. At the time when the Huikang Steamer struck the reef, its first and second holds were breached by the submerged reef. The forward hold and the first hold suddenly flooded, causing danger. At this time, the ship was unable to move. Shanghai only received the shipowner's urgent telegram requesting rescue at 4:00 PM yesterday. The original telegram stated: "Huikang departed Quanzhou for Xiamen yesterday, hit submerged reef at Quanzhou port at 5:00 AM, first and second holds flooded, ran aground immediately due to danger, please send rescue ship quickly." There are 430 tons of loaded cargo in the hold.

Rapidly Ran Aground. After the ship flooded, the shipowner, seeing that the situation was critical and fearing that it would sink at sea, immediately steered the Huikang Steamer towards the shallow waters off the northern coast of Dazhui Island to ground the ship. The depth of the water at high tide is 18 feet 2 inches, and at low tide it is 6 feet. The draft of the Huikang Steamer is 8 feet 7 inches forward and 12 feet 9 inches aft. The hull of the forward hold has been breached in two places.

Rescue Efforts. After receiving the report in Shanghai, in addition to notifying the China Ship Insurance Joint Association, the shipowner and agent in Quanzhou were urgently telegraphed, ordering them to dispatch barges to unload the cargo in case it was necessary. Mr. Lu Huichuan, general manager of Huitong Company in Shanghai, also discussed with the Insurance Joint Association and quickly dispatched a rescue ship to the scene. Director Tang of the China Ship Insurance Joint Association agreed last night to send workers with cement materials to the scene to first repair the breached holes in the ship before towing it away.

Ship Condition. The Huikang Steamer was built in Italy in 1902. The hull is steel, the gross tonnage is 1599 tons, the registered tonnage is 936 tons, the length is 258 feet, the width is 24 feet, the depth is 22 feet, the draft is 17 feet 4 inches, it has three decks, the machinery is a triple expansion type, the horsepower is 850, the steam pressure is 180, and it can travel at 10.5 nautical miles per hour. The ship has a peace of mind insurance policy of 80,000 yuan with the China Ship Insurance Joint Association.

At around 8:00 PM, three robbers suddenly entered the Huichangxiang Tailor Shop at No. 1222 Zhonghua Road, Xiaoximen, Nanshi. Lectures on Traditional Chinese Medicine Supplementary Subjects Published 139

This book was compiled by Ding Fubao and is divided into three parts: Physiology and Hygiene, Medicine, and Treatment. The Physiology and Hygiene part describes the outline of physiology and hygiene. The Medicine part has a total of thirteen chapters, with extremely detailed explanations of the causes and course of various diseases, and precise theories. The Treatment part includes treatments such as drugs, clinical medicine, physics, immunity, and first aid, all of which are practical. The whole book integrates the old and the new, and is clear and accessible, which is very suitable for beginners and as a supplementary reading for traditional Chinese medicine. Moreover, the price is low, the entire two volumes are only sold at the actual price of one yuan, and are sold at the Medical Bookstore at No. 204 Meibaige Road, Shanghai.

Sports News

1935-1936 Men's Basketball Rules Changes 147

Announced by the China National Amateur Athletic Federation

Article 5 of Chapter 1: The free throw area arc is to be marked with a dotted line and extended into a full circle. This free throw circle is to restrict other players from standing close to the jumpers when the jump ball takes place on the free throw line. The entire text is changed as follows:

The free throw area is marked at both ends of the court. Each area is divided by two straight lines six feet apart, parallel to and equidistant from the sidelines of the court. One end of the two parallel lines intersects the end line of the court. The other end connects to a large arc with a radius of six feet. The center of the circle should be equidistant from the sidelines on both sides of the court and seventeen feet from the inside edge of the end line of the court. The small arc of the circle (the arc drawn in the middle of the two parallel lines) should be a dotted line.

Article 3 of Chapter 5: Add a section after the note to avoid delays when substituting players. The full text is as follows:

To facilitate players in identifying their opponents, when a substitute enters the court, they should report their number and position to the referee or inspector. If possible, the number of their opponent should not be reported. The substitute may speak with the player being substituted to ask who their opponent is. The purpose of this note is to prevent common errors and delays during substitutions.

Article 10 of Chapter 7 modifies the definition of "dribbling." A ball that falls from the hand or an action to obtain the ball does not count as dribbling. That is, after the ball leaves the hand or is tapped out of a crowd, a player may start dribbling. If the player has a better chance of getting the ball this way, but deliberately moves the ball forward after getting it, it should be considered a walk. The full text is as follows:

After a player obtains the ball, throwing, tapping, or rolling the ball and then touching the ball again before it is touched by another person is called "dribbling." When dribbling, the ball must touch the ground except for one "air dribble." That is, when a player starts dribbling, they may throw the ball into the air, or during dribbling, they may tap the ball into the air once with their hand. Before the ball lands, they may touch the ball again.

After the above action, if the player touches the ball with both hands simultaneously or stops the ball in one hand or both hands, the dribble ends. When the hand is not touching the ball, the player may run an unlimited number of steps. Between each two taps of the ball during dribbling, the player may run at will, without being limited in the number of steps.

(Note) The following examples are not considered dribbling:

(1) Continuing to shoot (i.e., consecutive shots), (2) A ball that falls from the hand, (3) A ball tapped from the hands of another player, (4) Tapping the ball out when trying to get the ball in a crowd, (5) Intercepting a pass and gaining possession. Article 1 of Chapter 8 changes the break time for games of ten minutes per half to fifteen minutes, but it may be reduced to ten minutes if both sides agree. The text of the first two sections is revised as follows:

At the start of the game, the referee or inspector should throw the ball up between two opposing players in accordance with the provisions of Articles 5 and 6 of this chapter. College-age team games should be divided into two halves, each half lasting twenty minutes, with a fifteen-minute break between the halves. If both sides agree, the break time may be reduced to ten minutes.

Add two sentences after Article 6 of Chapter 8. The full text is as follows:

Other players should each stand at a reasonable distance from the jumper and the referee (or inspector) before the ball is touched by the jumper.

When jumping on the free throw line, all players except the jumpers should stand outside the free throw circle before the ball is touched.

Note to Article 1 of Chapter 10: If the space outside the boundary line of the court is less than three feet, a dotted line should be drawn three feet inside the line to restrict guarding players from standing too close when throwing the ball in from out of bounds. The full text is as follows: If the space outside the boundary line of the court is less than three feet, both players should stand more than three feet away from the thrower. A clear dotted line should be marked three feet inside the boundary line of the court.

Add a sentence after Section 4 of Article 1 of Chapter 11. The full text is as follows:

Players who are disqualified from the game may also be given a reasonable amount of time.

Part of Section 5 of Article 1 of Chapter 11 has been changed. The full text is as follows:

For all other types of foul free throws, the time should be counted from the moment the foul occurs until the ball is thrown in from out of bounds, crossing the boundary line.

Free Throw, Chapter 13, the first sentence of Article 5: This is an important change within these rules. After a free throw for a personal foul is made, play continues with a throw-in from out of bounds. The full text is as follows:

If a free throw for a personal foul is made, a player from the free thrower's opposing team should throw the ball into the court from any point outside the end line to continue the game. If it is a series of free throws, the above rule only applies to the last free throw. After a double foul or one or more technical fouls, regardless of whether the last free throw is made or not, the ball should be jumped in the center circle, except in the circumstances mentioned in Article 6. (To be continued)

First Battle of the Public Exhibition Cup: Western Youth Slightly Superior 149

Winning 3-1 Overall, Today's Four Singles Matches

The 7th International Public Exhibition Cup Handball Tournament opened at the Western Youth Stadium at 5:45 PM yesterday. Five singles matches were originally scheduled, but Hua Fenggang was unable to participate due to unforeseen circumstances. With the consent of both sides, it was changed to be held today. In yesterday's four matches, China only won one. The defeats in the first and third matches were the most regrettable. However, there are still six singles matches and five doubles matches in the first round. If the Chinese team can give their all, it should not be difficult to quell the arrogant foreign team.

Hong Yukui's Great Delight

Yesterday's matches were the 7th, 3rd, 1st, and 9th groups. Hong Yukui of the 7th group played against Banairnal first. Hong is one of the mainstays of the Chinese Youth team, repeatedly defeating strong opponents. He once won the Shanghai Chinese Open Championship. Last year, he partnered with Zhu Kuan to win the Shanghai Doubles Open Championship. He is young and strong, so Banairnal was no match for him. After coming on the court, he used his bold and sweeping strokes, like a hot knife through butter, winning two games in a row with scores of 21-17 and 21-12, winning as easily as turning his hand.

Yan Peiqiu's Skill is High, But Strength is Weak

Yan Peiqiu of the third group played against Lakimbi. Lakimbi is known as a "sticky candy," while Yan is superior in skill, so their strengths are considered equal. The score of the first game was very close. Yan only won at 22-20. Starting in the second game, Yan fell behind 12-19 and used his skills to fight back hard, tying the game at 19. Just when he expected to be smooth sailing, he exhausted himself by being too brave. Lakimbi won two points in a row, making it one game each. After a short rest, each side exerted their full strength in the decisive third game. Yan started smoothly, taking an 18-13 lead. At the crucial moment, Yan suddenly had a leg cramp, greatly weakening his strength. He was countered by Lakimbi, who won the third game 21-19. It can be said that it was extremely unfortunate.

Zhu, the King of Balls, Lost Due to Underestimation

Zhu Kuan in the handball world is like Li Huitang in the football world, while Ke Klin is also a main player for Western Youth. The competition must be fierce when two heroes meet. However, after the start of the first game, Zhu lost the first game due to excessive underestimation. In the second game, Zhu showed off his smashing and pressing skills, scoring 21-5 to retaliate. In the crucial third game, Zhu took a 19-16 lead. Just when victory seemed to be in his grasp, bad luck struck. Ke Klin repeatedly used dangerously low balls to tie the score. The last two balls were so dangerous that they could not be saved by human power. The best winning situation was wasted, resulting in a miserable defeat. Zhu is known as a victorious general, and it is easy to imagine his frustration after this setback.

Western Youth Leads 3-1

The Chinese team suffered two consecutive blows, and their morale was low. Sun Baoqi in the ninth group then took the field against Bai Xu. Sun shouted loudly and was exceptionally brave. He repeatedly escaped danger in the first game, using clever tricks to defeat Bai Xu, making Bai Xu shake his head and concede defeat. The second game was even more tense. Sun fought calmly, repeatedly taking the lead. However, in the second half of the game, Bai Xu steadily pressed forward, while Sun's strength gradually declined, and he finally lost. It became a tie. In the third game, he was exhausted. Although he tried his best, it was difficult to save the situation, and he was defeated 2-1 by Bai Xu. In summary, Western Youth led 3-1 after the first day of competition. The results of each game and today's schedule are as follows:

Admission Information for the University of Michigan, USA 160

Published by the Global Student Association

The University of Michigan is one of the famous universities in the central United States. The school has beautiful scenery, which is very suitable for studying and living, and the cost is cheap. Therefore, in recent years, many domestic students have gone to study at the school. The Global Student Association in Shanghai has previously investigated the school's general situation. Yesterday, it specially published the Admission Information for the Graduate School of Political Science of the University of Michigan, which was compiled and described, for the reference of those who are interested in studying at the school.

Requirements for a Master's Degree

(3) Special requirements for a master's degree in this department: A. Language: Anyone who wants to study for a master's degree in this department must first have the knowledge of reading French or German. In special circumstances, with the consent of the advisor of this department, another foreign language can be used instead. This language test is handled by the advisor of this department. B. Thesis: Anyone who wants to study for a master's degree in this department must write a master's thesis. After registration, each student must select a thesis topic as soon as possible, and at the same time consult with the senior student of this department, and be guided by him to complete it. Each student's topic and the name of the senior student of this department must be reported to the advisor of this department. Each student's thesis must be submitted to the advisor of this department before May 15 at the end of the second semester. If you are a first-semester student, submit it by January 15. If you are a summer student, submit it at least two weeks before the end of the summer. The submitted thesis must be bound in two copies, one of which must be bound with a black cover in accordance with the format specified by this department. This copy is kept by this department. All selected theses must be approved in writing by the senior student in charge of guiding the student's work and another senior student of this department. C. Examination: Anyone who wants to obtain a master's degree in this department must undergo a general examination in any subject. The subjects of this examination are selected by each senior student. This department does not conduct a broad master's examination.

Requirements for Research Work

(1) General Principles: The general principles of graduate school work at the University of Michigan can be found in the Graduate School's Announcement. All graduate students in the Department of Political Science should be familiar with these general principles. (2) Registration and Inquiry: Students who want to register for the Graduate School of Political Science must follow the regulations in the Announcement and ask Professor White Long, the advisor of this department, in Room 2023 of the Siji Building for details. After the registration time, Professor White Long will discuss everything with graduate students who have registered for admission or those who are interested in studying political science. The first semester will be held on Mondays and Wednesdays at 10:00 am. The second semester will be held on Mondays and Thursdays at 10:00 am. When necessary, it will be convened temporarily in Room 2032 of the Siji Building. At the end of the first semester, each graduate student must gather in front of the faculty of this department on the scheduled date to jointly discuss each person's work.

Requirements for a Doctoral Degree

(4) Special requirements for a Ph.D. degree in this department: A. The special requirements for a Ph.D. degree in this department are determined by the committee in charge of the student's work. B. Examination: Anyone who wants to take the examination for a Ph.D. degree in this department must discuss with each committee member and the advisor of graduate students in this department about the scope of the examination that each student is willing to take. However, the subject of political theory is the main compulsory subject for all students. In addition, three or four items can be added from the following items: American national government and constitution, provincial government and state government, municipal government, American government and European governments, Far Eastern governments, colonial governments, political parties, international law and international relations, history, economics, society, and other similar sciences. Each student must also choose one or two items to supplement it. The general examination of this department is usually held in two parts before each student completes his thesis. This examination is often an oral examination, but the committee may also hold a written examination if necessary. In addition to the subjects that each student has studied, other abilities to understand political science issues and specialized knowledge of literature must be examined. Students must also independently and clearly express their own abilities, with clear expression. The scope of each student's thesis will be kept as the final examination material. When this examination is held, each student should make a statement about his thesis, test his awareness of his thesis, and agree with the committee on the date of the examination. However, it must not be later than the date of the general examination of the school stipulated in the regulations, or when the summer school is held. C. Language: Each student must take a language test before taking the general examination. D. Required courses: Political Science 29's books and research methods are compulsory subjects for all students who want to obtain a doctorate degree in the first academic year. Graduate students of this department must also participate in the Political Science Book Report Research Association and its proceedings.

It Is Not True That Universities in Peiping and Tianjin Are Moving South 163

The Tax College Had Already Moved to Shanghai and Merged

Xin Sheng News Agency said, "The Daily" reported that universities in Peiping and Tianjin were preparing to move south. Yesterday, an authority on education in Shanghai confirmed that it was absolutely untrue. This is actually a rumor to confuse people. The government and the school authorities in Peiping and Tianjin have no such preparations. It is said that the four specialized schools, such as the Peiping Taxation School, have decided to move south. However, it is not known that the Peiping Taxation School has already moved south to Shanghai to enrich the school affairs and merge with the branch school for more than half a year.

Director Pan of the Education Bureau Returned to Shanghai Yesterday 164

Pan Gong Zhan, the newly appointed member of the Central Committee and Director of the Education Bureau of the city, went to Beijing on the 15th of this month to attend the Fifth National Congress. Now that he has completed his official duties, he returned to Shanghai yesterday morning, and immediately went to the Education Bureau to attend the Memorial Week. He is also scheduled to go to Beijing at the end of the month to attend the First Plenary Session of the Central Committee. Xu Ze Xiang, the Director of the Municipal Library, and others also returned yesterday.

The Municipal Education Bureau Commends Fifteen Schools, Including Xiude, for Achieving First-Class Results 165

The Municipal Education Bureau inspected the performance of private schools in Shanghai in the second semester of the 23rd year of the Republic. The schools that were rated as first-class include Xiude, Si Sheng, Jing An, Zhou Guang, Gan Gong, Cheng Zhong, Dun Hua, Zhong Zhen, Far East, San Yu, Ling Nan, Ningbo Second, Guang Gong Second, Qin De Girls', and Ming De Girls' Elementary School, a total of fifteen schools. It is said that the Bureau has issued an order to commend them to encourage them.

Children's Educational Novel

Little Men (106) 166

— Original by Louisa M. Alcott, translated by Zheng Xiao Cang

So he went away, smiling, high on his mother's shoulder, with a drowsy sweetness that made him perfectly irresistible.

But when the evening talk was all done, and the sweet songs were all sung, and the house was full of the Sunday quiet that always seemed to have a flavor of its own, Don lay awake in his cozy room, thinking over the new thoughts, and feeling the stir of new hopes and desires in his little heart; for the good angels, Love and Gratitude, had come in; and, having Time and Patience to help them, would surely do their work well. Earnest to keep his vow, Don clasped his small hands in the dark, and softly repeated Tanty's short prayer:

"God bless everybody, and make me good."

CHAPTER VII. LOST.

ONE fine autumn afternoon the Plumfield Square echoed with the clatter of tin pails, the tramp of excited feet, and the sound of children's voices, clamoring for something to eat,—for the boys and girls were going blackberrying on the Great Meadow, and were making their preparations with as much bustle as if they were about to start on a voyage of discovery.

"Now, my dears, go quietly, and don't let Rob see you, if you can help it," said Mrs. Jo, as she tied a wide-brimmed hat over little Nan's curly head.

Yesterday, the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange was on the last day of futures trading for this month. Due to the sudden deterioration of the situation in North China, people were quite worried. New York Stock Closing Shows Unusual Activity 171
