Spring and Autumn

Tidbits 183

— (Xiao Bai)

Two robbers, as they happened to pass a gallows, one of them said with seeming fear, "If there were no such instruments of torture as gallows in the world, how happy would our profession be!" The other robber coldly replied, "Bah! Your view is wrong. You must know that it is precisely our benefactor, because if there were no such things as gallows in the world, then everyone would be doing our job, and our business would become impossible."

A novice writer, submitting his manuscript to the editor, often encounters rejection or is thrown into the paper shredder, but this has also created many famous writers. Therefore, "failure" is enough to awaken a person's potential, push him to realize his potential, and enable him to achieve his goal.

We should not fear hardship and sorrow, and seek to escape, but should strive to turn all "disappointments" into "assistance," just as ants can transform annoying sand grains into pearls.

Beneath the Tomb of Manshu 184

— Shu Fan

To call West Lake a scenic area is better to rename it a historic site. Because every temple, bridge, mountain, and flower in that place is named after people. Heroes like Yue Fei, Yu Qian, and Zhang Cangshui, recluses like Lin Bu, Jiang Baishi, Fan Xie, and Jin Nong; even minor figures like the beauties Su Xiaoxiao and Xiaoqing, all leave behind a lasting charm, adding color to the lake and mountains. Therefore, people who travel today invariably mention Wulin: driving around to express feelings is surely not solely for sightseeing. Speaking of the shrines and tombs on the lake, they are also increasing daily, but it is a pity that those whom modern people admire may not be those whom later generations greatly admire. In that case, seek out Manshu. According to Xuan Ying, he waved gold about, dissipated sorrow with beauties, hid as a monk, yet remained somewhat constrained by the words and actions of a monk; only one with good knowledge and great determination could do this. Therefore, when I read his collected works, I am not surprised by his poetry, but I absolutely adore his person and deeds. It is already bitter enough for a scholar to withdraw from society due to frustration. Yet, he could not retreat to a tranquil and solitary state; the pent-up resentment in his heart must have been more than three dou's worth of grievances. If someone were to use him, to bring out what he held within, the feeling of sorrow and weeping could possibly be transformed into policies that would benefit the people. "Looking out, the land is full of useless men, in robes, tears before the stele." "Thank you, Liu San, for the news, I still have a small life to be a poet monk." However, those who understood him in the world were only Liu San; those who could be told were the heroes of past generations, but there was no one to confide in. Thus, he wandered the world, ending in depression. His fate was unfortunate, and his person was thus all the more worth remembering. The tomb is located on the shady side of Gushan, a few hundred paces from Xiling Bridge, and those who tour the lake often pass by. I used to stay by the lake and, during vacations, would drive there every day, leaning on the grass and rubbing the stele, often not returning until the moon rose. Sometimes I would hear the bell of Fenglin Monastery emerging from the edge of the forest, and facing this mound of earth, I would feel the awe of what era this was! "The dust of ages is viewed like this, gather the remaining tears to await a clear time." I do not know for whom this is made? This autumn, I once again spoke with Meng Jiao in the dark about it, thinking that the grass on the tomb must be fine, while we have both reached middle age; the stars were like rain, and clear sounds erupted, does the person in the tomb know? To express feelings with a poem, why must it be said for him? "Covered in autumn dew, watching the stars, a pestle, vast tracks of dust. The daily lesson, the monk laughs to himself, how could he have thought someone was listening to the bell?"

Anecdotes of the Executioner 185

— Wang Shouqiu

Everyone knows that an executioner is someone who kills people. Because in the past, during the monarchical era, all executions of criminals were carried out by beheading. Beheading required an executioner! It is said that an executioner's beheading, like other professions, requires practice. Their method of practicing is to use large steamed buns to test their skill. With one strike, the upper half of the bun must roll off. And they draw a black line on the bun, and the blade must be aligned with this black line. At first, it is naturally not accurate. But over time, they can be perfect, and then they can become executioners and be competent and happy.

According to old people, an executioner can only kill with one strike. If the person does not die with one strike, they cannot strike a second time. Therefore, executioners must be well-trained before they dare to go to the execution ground. I remember hearing a story like this: "A robber was caught by the authorities. Because he had committed many crimes, he was naturally unforgivable and was sentenced to death. His wife was beautiful, and their relationship was very good. So she always wanted to save him. So she sacrificed her body to get to know the executioner and said, 'Unfortunately, I have a robber husband, and although he is about to be executed, it is already too late! If the executioner is willing to have me, I am willing to be his wife forever.' The executioner was of course willing. The night before her husband's execution, she told the executioner, 'My husband's braid is very good. Please cut it off for me tomorrow to make a wig.' The executioner was already infatuated with her and naturally obeyed her orders. So the next day, when he killed her husband, he first cut off his braid. Just as he was about to cut his neck, the robber's wife suddenly ran out of the crowd and shouted that he had already been struck once! The supervising officer had no choice but to immediately let the robber down and had this executioner represent him and had another executioner behead him! At this time, although the executioner knew he had been greatly deceived, it was already too late!"

Crises Everywhere! 186

Land Marriage 187

— Fang Zheng

I remember just a few days ago! The second page of this newspaper carried an article by Mr. Feng Zikai about a double life, saying, "...On the one hand, the newspaper publishes divorces, on the other hand, it is building chastity arches... Next to new-style cars, there will also be sedan chairs carried by four people. This is the so-called double life of the Chinese..." But what I am recording here is even better than a double life! The facts are like this.

On the tenth of this month, our small rural town—Yinxiang Port—suddenly became lively. The general male and female villagers, young and old, each held a stick of incense with great devotion, crowding in the crowd, almost breaking this narrow little street. If you want to use an adjective to describe them, then only "a sea of people" is worthy of it. Such excitement is only the first time in our small town! But the reason for the excitement is indeed difficult to guess. Later, I asked someone on the inside (the initiator of this matter), who said: "The Land God is getting married!"

"Ah! It's really strange. Only people have marriages. How can the Bodhisattva get married? Could it be a joke?" I asked him incredulously, and he told me a strange story:

"There is a Land Temple on the north side of the Wang Family Guanyin Hall in this town. There is a Bodhisattva inside. Because it has gained the belief of the general villagers, people often go to burn incense and worship. On the 27th of last month, a young girl also went to burn incense. When she finished worshiping, just as she stood up, she suddenly smiled. Unexpectedly, the Bodhisattva took a fancy to her. Sure enough, the girl got sick and died soon after returning home. Because of this reason, her mother suspected that she must have been taken by the Land God to be his concubine. So she made this wooden statue for her and chose today (a good day) to marry them both."

When I finished listening to this strange story, I couldn't help but sigh repeatedly, not only lamenting the villagers' pitiful superstition, but also that at a time when rural areas are bankrupt and markets are exhausted, there should not be such pointless actions. But we Chinese are not like that! No matter how loudly people shout "get rid of superstition," they are always dreaming of superstition. But this is not that era now. It's really sad to say; the day before yesterday, the Boy Scouts of the Flood Relief Association came to this town to raise donations, but they didn't get a single penny. But today's event, just the consumption of incense alone, reached several hundred yuan! How can the Chinese not be poor? How can they not be bullied?

Little Western Paradise 188

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 22: Gently Relying on Someone, Over the Courtyard, Pitying the Moon's Beauty, Passionately Instructing the Son-in-Law, Listening to the Lion's Roar from the Next Room

As for economic matters, that would be a joke. I'm afraid you don't understand what a monetary system or a gold standard is. You just know that goods pass in front of your office, and you collect a few coins from people. I fundamentally despise you. If it weren't for the money, I wouldn't have come to find you even if we hadn't been in touch for ten years. After this scolding, Bei Hai was also stunned. Is there a wife who scolds her husband like this? Zhi Qian also shook his head a few times and smiled at Bei Hai. Bei Hai was about to say something, but Zhi Qian waved his hand at him and pointed to the room next door, meaning to tell him to listen down there. So the two of them looked at each other and listened to the next room. The director, after receiving this scolding, seemed unable to bear it and let out a short, sharp sound, replying: "Are these the words you're saying to me? It was very difficult for me to take leave and come to Xi'an to pick you up. Now you want me to get the money, and after I get the money, you want me to send it to you. This round trip will take so much effort. If my superiors find out and cancel my job, I'm naturally finished. What advantage can you gain? If you still plan to ask for thousands of dollars, then kill me, and I still can't get it out! If you want to get the money, then you have to go to Gansu with me." The sound of these words came from far to near and was very similar to the way the woman spoke. While speaking, he heard the woman put something down, heavily hitting the table with a bang, and then said: "Okay, as long as you can get the money, I will go to Gansu with you. Don't be like this, get away." There was a sound of staggering footsteps, and the man dragged out his voice and said: "That place can't compare to Xi'an. You eat black steamed buns, drink mud water, and there aren't even green vegetables and radishes..." (366)

Small Recipes

Filling Dishes with Flowers and Fruits 189

— Yi Mei

Food is one of the four essential elements of life and cannot be interrupted for a single day. All the treasures of the mountains, the delicacies of the sea, the running of the beasts, and the flying of the birds are all gathered to satisfy the appetite. How great is mankind's insatiable desire for food! However, there are also those who pick flowers and fruits to make delicacies, which are exceptionally refined and delightful. According to my knowledge, I will haphazardly record some on the left:

1. Stuffed Lotus Root: Peel the lotus root and cut it into thin slices. Grind the meat into a paste, mix in sesame oil, salt, flour, etc., and sandwich it between two slices of lotus root. Deep fry it in a frying pan until golden brown, then remove it and eat it with sweet sauce. It has a unique flavor.

2. Jade Embryo Soup: Li Mei'an's family recipe has a Jade Embryo Soup. The method is to make a soup with late winter jade (a type of mushroom) and Yunnan bamboo shoots. The shoots are tender and the jade is fragrant, creating two wonderful flavors.

3. Snow Pear Chicken: Slaughter the chicken and take the meat, cutting it into thin slices. Stir-fry it three or four times in lard, then add sesame oil and stir-fry it again. Then add salt, pepper powder, and pear slices and rock sugar, and it is ready. The taste is extremely crisp and refreshing.

4. Pumpkin Cake: Pumpkin flowers can also be cooked and eaten. When I lived in a certain family, I once picked a number of flowers in the early morning, mixed them with flour and cane sugar, and fried them in boiling oil until they were slightly charred. I scooped them out, put them on a plate to serve as snacks, and tasted them. They were rich, delicious, sweet, and fragrant beyond description. At that time, the old painter Bing He was also present and praised them endlessly, saying that such a good taste should be described by you to make up for the shortcomings of the ancient people's food recipes.

5. Watermelon Duck: Choose a round watermelon, cut off its top, scoop out the pulp, place duck and slices of southern ham, tender bamboo shoots, dried scallops, and winter mushrooms inside. Add yellow wine and salt, seal it with mulberry paper, steam it in a pot over water until cooked through. It is rich, fragrant, and delicious, an unparalleled delicacy for summer family dishes.

6. Blanched Magnolia Petals: Pick magnolia buds and remove the petal tips. Separately use flour and white sugar, mix in chicken eggs, and mix evenly with chopsticks. Soak the magnolia petals in it, then blanch them in a sesame oil pan until they are dry and crispy.

7. Osmanthus Eggs: Use chicken eggs, diced ham, and osmanthus sauce and stir-fry them together. Those who like sweet flavors can add rock sugar, and those who like salty flavors can add salt. This is a famous dish in Zhangde, Henan Province.

8. Chestnut Chicken: First boil the chicken pieces until they are golden brown, add yellow wine, soy sauce, and chestnuts to the pot, cover and simmer. Finally, add white sugar and remove from the pot immediately.

9. Chrysanthemum Shark Fin: Use washed shark fin, taking the soft spines. Next, boil the chicken until cooked, taking only the skin. Then cut the meat into shreds, stir-fry it in an oil pan, add yellow wine and soy sauce, and braise it with cabbage until cooked. Then wrap the shark fin in the chicken skin, add it to the stew, and cover it with fresh chrysanthemum threads. The taste is both fragrant and the color is beautiful. Cantonese restaurants are best at making this dish.

10. Hawthorn Jelly: Use one or two pieces of hawthorn cake, add white sugar, cocoa, and osmanthus sauce, then pour boiling water over it. Served occasionally at the edge of a banquet, it is refreshing and unparalleled.

11. Cherry Blossom Dumplings: At the beginning of summer and the end of spring, people in the Japanese archipelago use cherry blossom leaves to wrap rice cakes, giving it a unique flavor.

12. Lotus Leaf Zha: According to Wu Xing's anecdotes: "In late autumn, the people on the lake make Li Zha. Small fish are added with spices and rice flour, wrapped in lotus leaves, and called Lotus Leaf Zha."

13. Water Chestnut Rice: Wu people must add some water chestnuts to the New Year's Eve dinner and cook them together to symbolize digging for treasure, a comical obsession with wealth.

14. Almond Tofu: Western restaurants have a color of almond tofu, made by boiling almond paste in tofu, mixing it with sugar juice, and storing it in the refrigerator. It is sweet, fragrant, and delicious, and is a good product for cooling off in summer.

15. Fox Nut Congee: Grind fox nuts into powder, cook it with double bow rice, add a little rock sugar, and it is sweet and delicious.

16. Grape Soup: Take purple grapes, peel off their skins, and mix them with sugar syrup to make grape soup. In the autumn of a certain year during the Guangxu reign of the late Qing Dynasty, the Japanese poet Oka Rokumon visited the two gentlemen Xu Huanong and Cai Fuchen in Beijing. Fuchen invited him to drink, and among the snacks was grape soup. Oka Rokumon asked about the history of grapes, and Huanong imitated the ancient people's practice of alluding to events with melon eating, and improvised twenty-eight rhymes to show him.

17. Lychee Duck: Use a clay pot, spread the bottom with lychee meat, season the slaughtered duck, place it on top of the lychees, cover it with lotus leaves, steam it over water for two hours, and then you can take it out and eat it.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talks

A Large Number of Prisoners Released on Parole from Caohejing Prison 190

— Meng Ruo

The Jiangsu Second Prison in Caohejing, Shanghai, is well-equipped and large-scale. It houses more than two thousand inmates. There are more than twenty men's and women's workshops. Recently, due to the gradual increase in the number of criminals, there has been a problem of overcrowding. In order to alleviate the prison, the authorities specially followed the order of the Ministry to organize parole. The first batch of more than one hundred people who were approved for parole have been released for many days. The second and third batches of more than one hundred people have been submitted to the High Court and the Garrison Headquarters. The fourth and fifth batches of more than three hundred people have been selected and are rushing to handle the review procedures and will be issued soon. It is estimated that there will be six or seven hundred prisoners who can be paroled this time. A parole ceremony was held, and the warden gave a speech. The prisoners were all awed and delighted.

The imperfection of China's judicial situation is an undeniable fact. The authorities, in view of this, have recently been quite determined to make up for various shortcomings. The promulgation of the regulations for alleviating prisons is one example. Imprisoning criminals is originally a kind of punishment for lawbreakers. And the intention of legislation is nothing more than to make criminals able to change their ways and become good after being punished. Therefore, civilized countries in the world all take a tolerant attitude towards criminals. Some use education to influence them, or implement parole to listen to their repentance, which is the best way. Now that prisons in our country also have this parole initiative, it is a good phenomenon.

In addition, in prisons throughout our country, except for a few large cities, where new-style prisons have been established, most of the old-style prisons are poorly equipped, and sanitation management is far from perfect. Moreover, the scale of prisons is small, and there are many prisoners. The suffering suffered by prisoners can truly be described as human hell. Especially in recent years, due to the impact of the social downturn, the number of criminals has increased day by day, and prisons everywhere are unable to accommodate them. Therefore, the act of parole is indeed necessary to be fully implemented. Parole can not only alleviate the congestion of prisoners, but also prevent unexpected events from occurring in guardianship. The fact that it is beneficial to the health and nutrition of prisoners is a secondary matter.

Moreover, so-called parole is to select prisoners in prison who have committed less serious crimes, or whose behavior is in line with the rules after entering prison, and who have a tendency to improve, before they are allowed to be released. It is better to give these criminals their freedom than to detain them in prison. In foreign countries, the results of parole are very good. Therefore, we hope that the six or seven hundred prisoners released from Caohejing Prison this time will be able to change their behavior and become good citizens after their release.

It is heard that the Ministry of Judicial Administration believes that there are many juvenile crimes in our country. In the 21st year, there were a total of 3,004 admissions. In terms of criminal policy and prison system, these juvenile offenders should not be treated in the same way as adult offenders. Therefore, it has been decided to build separate prisons in important cities so that they can receive more complete education, so that they can become healthy young people after they are released from prison in the future. This news is very gratifying and must be considered a progress in the judicial world of our country.

Page 16

Miscellaneous Notes on the Elephant Kingdom 191

— Cong Long

Almost everyone who has lived in Siam for a long time feels a deep affection for Siam, especially for its beautiful scenery and interesting customs.

As the ship entered the winding Siamese Gulf, the speed slowed down, and the ship was like a sick elephant, crawling slowly on the lovely and shimmering green water. "Oh, it's arrived, arrived at the port of Siam!" it was shouted, and the whole ship was in turmoil.

On both sides of the green waves, two boundless coconut groves stretched out, towering into the clouds, lush green, connecting to the sky, blending with the jade-like blue sky. Looking through the oily green leaves of the coconut groves, one or two pointed pagoda tops could be seen from time to time, protruding from the gaps in the leaves, shining with brilliant golden color under the hot tropical sun, stabbing like thorns, how dazzling! This is the Siamese Buddhist temple.

In the shallow waters on both sides of the bank, many rows of wooden boats floated, standing still. These boats are a bit different from ordinary cargo ships: they have pavilions and are square. The boats are tightly fastened with thick iron cables, only allowing them to float and rise and fall with the tide, but refusing to let them change their position. This is the Siamese people's "Pa", - home on the water.

Siamese women, like the women of Calingga, expose their upper bodies, allowing their breasts, like new graves, to tremble, pointed and erect, walking on the street without any shyness, with a red and green "benlong" (skirt) wrapped around their lower bodies.

In the evening, after dinner, the sun set, and a remnant of sunlight remained on the horizon. At this time, without any boundaries, they slipped into the river naked. The river suddenly became lively, with the sound of splashing water and the giggling laughter intermingling.

"Splashing water" is very common in Siam, and in many places, it is considered a popular courtesy. Whenever new guests meet, regardless of gender, both parties must splash each other with cold water all over the body. As long as there is water available to splash, it is not enough to show affection if you do not do so. Even when encountering people you don't know at all, you can splash cold water on him (or her) unexpectedly and stand by the roadside laughing.

Water is one of the essential elements of life in Siam, and there is no need to say that the vast rice fields need a lot of water for irrigation. At the same time, because of the hot tropical climate, people cannot withstand the scorching sun and need to take many cool baths every day. As for after death, in addition to holding a cremation ceremony, there is also a so-called water-dripping ceremony, in which the stiff body of the dead person is placed in the house, and the right hand is pulled open. The visitors then walk around the deceased once and drip a few drops of holy water on the palm of the deceased's hand. Thus, the water-dripping ceremony is completed.

There is also a very interesting custom in Siamese men and women's marriage. In Jingmai, as long as a man who does not have a family, in order to seek marriage, he can arbitrarily break into any unfamiliar home. After explaining his intentions, the unmarried girl of that family must come out to sit and talk with him. At this time, the parents in the family avoid going to the outer room or go out, allowing them to talk in detail. If the woman is attracted to the other party, when she personally presents him with a betel leaf roll, the roll is made of two leaves, then it is considered to indicate her consent to the marriage. Then, the man can freely enter and exit the woman's house, sleep and eat at the woman's house, and be considered the woman's quick son-in-law.

I love Siam, I love the beauty and tranquility of its natural scenery; I love the generosity, simplicity, innocence, and unpretentious nature of its people!

Night Train 192

— Especially

The cold weather brought a dim sky, with a sinister face swallowing the ground.

The north is a plateau region, and the air is dry. Because of this, the warm and humid air of the nearby sea is not visible. After autumn inadvertently slips past in the eyes, the wind will howl. Perhaps the construction of civilization has not yet developed to a certain stage. On the muddy roads of the streets, gray sand runs along, howling like wolves or something else. It hits the rare glass window paper, with a whoosh, then another whoosh.

Guarding an oil lamp, searching around the room, this is worth cherishing, that is also worth cherishing. Although it's not worth much money, the home is about to be moved entirely. Facing all those old belongings, lined with the dim light of the lamp, a wave of desolation swept through the heart, bringing a shiver.

Yes, I'm reluctant to leave home, no, my hometown. I admire the simple and unsophisticated charm of my hometown that is praised by people.

How can that be allowed? Let the longing be hidden first! As before, I rummage through and pack things up.

In the cold weather, the night is long. When everything is ready, stepping out the door, the sky's face is still frighteningly black. Several letters have been prepared, lying on the lid of the suitcase. The window paper is stained with a trace of gray-white.

—Second Master, it's time to go. The train at the East Station leaves at seven o'clock! The pre-arranged rickshaw rushed in, looking somewhat flustered, as if blaming me for being too careless.

There was no time for farewells, so I hastily set off. The morning wind was truly sharp, hitting the face like a knife. The ground and rooftops were tightly covered with thick frost, like a wool carpet. The rickshaw puller's feet stepped on the unsolidified frost, making a croaking sound like a frog.

Following the train wheels, following that expanse of houses and grassland, the hometown disappeared into the heavy darkness.

Arriving in Tianjin, it was midday. I learned that the ship to Shanghai would not depart until the tide rose tomorrow. Moreover, the ship does not enter the port and still needs to go through a section of the Tianjin-Tangshan train. Alas, what a mess. Should I just stay at the station and wait for night? Or should I go to Tangshan to wait first? Hesitating for a long time, I finally accepted the inn's offer and went to the hostel first.

Half a day passed quickly, and the ship ticket was bought in advance.

Thankful for the kindness of the shopkeeper, he told me that it was best to leave around nine o'clock. It would take at most an hour to get to Tangshan, and then I could get on the ship right away. It was much better than waiting there for a long time. At the time, I thought this kindness was rare because for someone who had never traveled far, being guided on how to complete the journey ahead was more valuable than anything else.

Following the instructions, I jumped into the train bound for Tangshan at a little past nine o'clock. This section of the journey was not very long. If the ship could enter the port, there would be no need for this section of the train. The number of people on the train could be said to be very few. The tea attendant huddled around a small stove dozing off. Several gentlemen opened their bedding, covered their heads, and fell soundly asleep. Solemnity enveloped the train. Except for the sound of the wheels grinding against the tracks, occasionally mixed with a few whistles, there were no other sounds.

About a quarter of an hour later, the ticket inspector came, dragged the gentlemen out of their blankets, and asked them to abide by the rules. But in the blink of an eye, they lay down again, muttering incessantly.

He came to me and marked my ticket as usual. Turning around, he saw something in the rice bag.

—What is this? His tone was quite stern.

—A stove, a small one.

As if he had discovered some secret, he immediately reached out and opened the mouth of the sack to take a look:

—Has it been weighed?

No.

—No, this kind of thing needs to be weighed. He frowned and thought for a while: Then, buy a supplementary ticket!

—How much?

—Humph, about ×× catties, well, let's say two dollars and forty cents!

This was a blow. Although this small stove was my beloved, its purchase price was only two dollars. Now, I actually had to pay a shipping fee higher than the purchase price, so I was naturally unwilling to accept it casually.

—I don't have that much money, do whatever you want with it!

—Throw it out the window! He ordered a colleague. His face turned purple.

—That's fine, it saves me the trouble. I was very calm.

Perhaps he didn't expect me to have this move, and for a moment, he couldn't retort. Looking at his face, he looked very embarrassed.

Later, through persuasion from people on the train, a price of sixty cents was paid to pass the checkpoint.

After taking the money, his anger had not subsided. He opened the door and darted into another carriage.

A gust of cold wind brushed past, and I couldn't help but shiver a few times. Outside the glass window, it was pitch black. The whistle on the front of the train stretched out its voice and shouted.

Song Introduction 194

Frugality Song

(1) In the world, who doesn't desire wealth and status? If you don't plan ahead, how can daily expenses be determined? Establishment is most difficult, destruction is extremely rapid! Poverty leads to idleness, borrowing brings shame. Work hard and manage diligently, and you won't worry about food! Frugality is better than asking others, don't follow the trend of extravagance. Quickly end wastefulness, and sing the Frugality Song together.

(2) Don't say you're young, time is like a spinning wheel. If you can work diligently, you'll have enough warm clothes. When sons grow up, marriage is imminent, when daughters grow up, marriage is also approaching. Parents are getting old, and all kinds of expenses continue. When you need to pay, you must save in your spare time! I dare to tell the ladies, let's all advocate frugality, quickly end wastefulness, and sing the Frugality Song together.

The moon is faint, the wind is mournful, and the night fog is thick. A lamp is like water, and my heart is heavy. I sit alone facing the lonely lamp, my intestines about to break. My delicate eyebrows are locked, and tears are thick. I think I am like pear blossoms in the spring rain, lamenting my thin fate. I was wrongly matched for life, full of endless hatred. My husband is aimless and unemployed all day long. He's lost in the paper and gold, like in a dream. He turns day into night, indulging in prostitution and gambling. He only returns home late at night. He squanders money like dirt. He sells off the ancestral property. He doesn't think about the children growing up and needing to study. Now, pitifully, they are neglected at home. I have tried to persuade him several times, but sadly, my loyal words are taken as wind. Alas, I, from a family of scholars, a golden girl. I was spoiled and raised in my boudoir in my childhood. Now, I manage family affairs and do chores myself. In the evening, I still have to do needlework under the lamp. I stay up late guarding the door, full of endless hatred in the silent boudoir. Who can I confide my heartfelt thoughts to? I often fill my chest with tears when I am sad. He can glorify the lintel and revive the family. So that I don't have to worry so much.

Xu Lai's Fate in "Boatman's Daughter" 200

In these times, the society is in recession, and many promising young people have been forced into becoming bad people by the harsh environment, especially when the will is weak among young girls. In "Boatman's Daughter," Xu Lai was originally a pure girl, rowing a boat with her old father in West Lake every day, living a virtuous life. However, the beautiful West Lake was also affected by the economic recession, and the number of tourists was becoming increasingly scarce. Like other debtors, they could not repay the boat rental fees every month. Under the fierce pressure of the boat owner, the fat Tan Zhihai, the old father was injured, and Xu Lai was also in the hands of the fat man. Finally, she became meat on the chopping block and became a goddess who sold her body. Every day, she endured whippings and hunger, enduring shame and humiliation, spending long years in sending off and welcoming guests. Is Xu Lai a goddess? No, she is just a weak woman who has been buried by the harsh environment!

Idle Talk about the Protagonist of "Long Live Love" 201

Hollywood's film tycoons are very aware that the public's tastes are constantly changing. Therefore, they are also constantly looking for new things to stimulate the public, and the selection of actors is no exception. Hifilai in the past, and the protagonist of "Long Live Love" (Here's to Romance), which will be released at the Grand Light Theater, Nie Nuo Matini, is a good example.

These two singers were brought to the United States from Europe by the film's producer, Ge Xi Lasi. Hifilai has already succeeded in becoming the only great lover on the screen with his relaxed performance and the style of jazz music. Now, when Hifilai returned to France, they thought of Matini, who had already become famous on the stage. Matini's singing voice can be called second to none after Caruso. Lasi therefore treated him as a new thing to stimulate the movie audience.

After the film was completed, it caused a sensation when it was released in the United States, and the ideal of the film tycoon was realized again. In order to help Matini succeed, they also went to Europe to find several famous singers and dancers to co-star, creating a very perfect musical romance. The reason why it could cause a sensation was not accidental. In short, Matini built a great achievement on the silver screen with a new archetype.

What Kind of "Situation" Is It Now? 202

In a corner of Shanghai West, there is a tall and magnificent Western-style house, which is the residence of Sun Zhonggui, the compradore of the Huadeng Bank. This Sun compradore obtained the position of compradore of the Huadeng Bank with a large amount of cash obtained from rent as a guarantee. However, his power is so great that it is truly red-hot.

His neighbor Zhao Dexiong is the general manager of the Zhenxing Yarn Factory and also a hero in the business world. He and Sun Zhonggui have a good relationship through marriage. Later, Dexiong's yarn factory suffered from foreign invasion, and its business plummeted. Although Dexiong struggled hard, he could not reverse the crisis. He had to discuss with Sun Zhonggui to mortgage the factory building to Huadeng Bank and borrow foreign capital to save the situation. As for the harsh contract conditions, although Dexiong had a marriage relationship with him, Zhonggui, because of the great interest involved, did not care. Not only that, Zhonggui also had sinister plans and secretly planned to seize his yarn factory.

The above story is only a small part of the dark side of the current society described in the giant sound production "Heroes of the Hour" by Yihua. However, we can use this to understand what kind of "situation" it is now. In fact, it is not only a snobbish "situation," a "situation" of the survival of the fittest," but also a treacherous "situation" full of selfishness and profit-seeking. As for these, the "Heroes of the Hour" will tell you in more detail, so you can understand the crimes of society and the treachery of people's hearts, as well as the crisis of the status of China's commercial and industrial industries in this play.

Shen Bao Architectural Weekly

A Brief Overview of the Construction of the Nanjing Martyrs' Cemetery by Fu Ji Construction Company 203

I. Introduction

The Martyrs' Cemetery includes the main gate, surrounding walls, memorial archway, memorial hall, memorial tower, and three cemetery plots.

This project was funded by the Central Party Headquarters in memory of the fallen heroes and was overseen by Committee Member Chen Guofu and others. It is located at the foot of Zhongshan Mountain in Linggu Temple, east of Dr. Sun Yat-sen's mausoleum, in a quiet and scenic area. Construction began in March of the 20th year of the Republic (1931) and was fully completed in May of the 23rd year of the Republic (1934). The commencement of construction was slightly delayed due to the architect's careful consideration of the model to make it lifelike and antique. Now that this solemn and magnificent project has been completed, the construction process is described in detail below.

II. Various Projects

A. Memorial Tower

The tower is octagonal, with nine stories, reaching a height of 200 English feet from the platform to the spire. A steel-reinforced concrete spiral staircase is located in the center, providing direct access to the ninth floor. Each floor has a surrounding veranda, enclosed by Su stone railings carved from single pieces, a very labor-intensive process. The interior beams and edge beams of each floor are painted with colored cement, which is an innovative alternative to the traditional painted decorations of Beijing. Ordinary paintings inevitably fade over time, but colored cement remains permanently unchanged; however, the initial mixing process was quite complex, requiring dozens of experiments before it was successfully completed. The proportion of yellow sand and cement to be mixed depends on the various colors; otherwise, cracks and color differences will inevitably appear after drying.

After determining the location, the excavation of the foundation began. The depth was required to be excavated according to the drawings until a large stone was found, but the excavation reached 14 feet deep without finding a whole stone. The excavation continued to 18 and a half feet, but the same result persisted, although the soil quality seemed to have been partially petrified and was very hard. After a detailed investigation of the slope of the rock strata by the engineer, it was determined that it was unknown where the rock layer could be found. A load-bearing test was conducted, and each square foot was able to carry more than four and a half tons, with no sinking even after a week. The engineer was satisfied, and this first step was completed. The concrete mixing was done by machine from the foundation to the top. The large platform around the base of the tower, with a diameter of 100 feet, is also octagonal; all paved with Su stone slabs, with steel-reinforced concrete underneath. The joints between the platform stone slabs and the concrete are fully filled with ice slurry, surrounded by Su stone railings; and there are four steps. In the center of the front, an extremely large plinth stone is inlaid; the Party emblem is carved on the top, and landscapes are engraved on the bottom, with three peaks representing the Three Principles of the People; and water representing freedom and equality. The engraving is incredibly detailed. All stone materials, whether made into smooth surfaces or railings, if any minor flaws or unevenness were found, our factory spared no expense and no effort to discard and redo them to ensure perfection; however, the size and number of pieces previously ordered were fixed, and if any were not suitable, a new order was inevitable; and extending the time was unavoidable.

The other roofs are covered with green Guangdong glazed tiles. The tiles were custom-made, and those with bright colors and no spots were selected for use to ensure uniform color. The top of the tower is made of cast iron, with the outside electroplated with real gold. The lightning rod at the top of the tower is made of pure purple copper in a three-pointed style, and eleven No. 16 wires are connected to the ground, with a two-square-foot purple copper plate connected to the other end of the lightning wire underground.

On the four large steles on the bottom floor of the tower are written the four characters "Jing Zhong Bao Guo" (Serve the Country Faithfully) in the handwriting of Chairman Chiang Kai-shek: the seven characters "Martyrs' Memorial Tower" on the horizontal plaque on the front are also in the handwriting of Chairman Chiang Kai-shek; showing his sincere love and respect for the loyal souls! Except for the lower floor, the remaining eight floors are inlaid with four stone tablets each, fully engraved with Dr. Sun Yat-sen's opening speech at Whampoa Military Academy, farewell speech, Chairman Chiang Kai-shek's preface to the Whampoa alumni roster, and posthumous list, all in the handwriting of modern celebrities.

The four large doors on the lower floor are framed with angle iron, covered with a whole piece of one-centimeter copper skin on the outside, and nailed with one-inch and six-minute semicircular copper nails.

B. Memorial Hall

Located in front of the tower, about 500 feet away, also in front of the old site of Zhi Gong Pagoda.

The hall is 136 feet and 6 inches long and 64 feet and 8 inches wide, with a long corridor around it, and the hall is in the style of a palace. The two-story roof is also covered with Guangdong glazed tiles, with painted beams and carved rafters; all imitating ancient palaces. The only difference is the distinction between wooden and cement beams and pillars. The completion date of the hall was nine months before the memorial tower. The interior materials and flat roof are the same as the memorial tower, so I will not repeat them here.

C. Memorial Hall

Formerly known as the Beamless Hall, later renamed the Immeasurable Hall, now named the Martyrs' Memorial Hall for Loyal Souls. It was originally a renovated old building, destroyed in the Taiping Heavenly Kingdom War. From its initial construction to the present, it has a history of more than 500 years. The committee, in order to preserve historical sites, specially renovated the hall and renamed it the Martyrs' Memorial Hall for Loyal Souls. The hall is 210 feet long and over 190 feet wide. Most of the front was already destroyed, and the roof was completely ruined; it has now been restored to its original appearance, solemn and magnificent; unparalleled. It is divided into three major circles, with the largest in the middle. All are made of ancient city bricks side-laid with one-to-two cement, covered with two-and-a-half-inch steel-reinforced concrete to connect them into one piece, and then a large beam is added every thirteen feet. The lower tunnel ring form: the upper follows the slope of the roof, the middle ring is about fifty feet high and more than forty feet wide, with no pillar support in the middle, hence the former name Beamless Hall. The roof tiles are also in the old style, covered with tiles sixteen feet long, seven feet wide, and six minutes thick, and the bottom tiles are the same length and thickness, fourteen feet wide, all black, custom-made in Suzhou. The floor is paved with twenty-foot square Beijing bricks, also custom-made in Suzhou. The windows and doors are cast from raw and cooked iron, sprayed with antique bronze color, using pure copper powder mixed with color, sprayed hot by machine; which can be maintained permanently. The walls inside and outside are plastered with lime, which cannot show the ancient bricks, so the old plaster was completely brushed off, and then the seams were filled with cement, so that the thickness of the ancient bricks can be shown. The lower half of the inner walls are inlaid with bluestone, fully engraved with the names of the martyrs.

D. Cemetery

The cemetery is divided into three parts: left, right, and center. The center is the largest, a circle with a radius of 192 feet, with a larger half circle and a smaller half circle added, the whole cemetery resembles a lotus flower. It was very difficult and time-consuming to measure and draw the lines: because the ground was full of weeds and trees. Once the location was determined, the excavation of the wall foundation began, and the standard was determined according to the height of the terrain; after the soil was excavated, lime and three-in-one soil in proportions of one, three, six, cement, etc. were laid. The wall surface project is made of pre-cast ice mud boards, with lengths of three, five, etc., and a thickness of four inches and a height of one foot. Each layer is built (the same on the back) with bricks inlaid in the middle, and then the second layer is built until the top, the construction method is the same. After the whole wall is built, the third step is carried out, and the inner and outer walls are cut into stone patterns, which can be called artificial stone. After the cemetery was completed, the remains of the martyrs since the Northern Expedition were buried in it.

E. Memorial Archway

Made of five tiers with six cement piers. The lower half is inlaid with carved Su stone, and the upper part is all artificial stone. When compacting the cement, one, two, and fine sand must be attached to the side of the formwork for several inches until the top is the same. The brackets are pre-cast, cut into artificial stone, and then placed. The top is also Guangdong glazed tiles.

F. Main Gate and Surrounding Walls

The main gate is a tunnel gate, the ground is fully paved with Su stone slabs, and a Su stone base. Next to it is a surrounding wall with a total length of more than 300 feet, with round doors at both ends. The east door has the plaque "Zhao Lie" (Showing Loyalty), and the west door has the plaque "Yang Zhong" (Promoting Loyalty). The whole wall is pink cement, and the top of the wall is covered with colored glazed tiles. The base is half Su stone and half starting stone. The materials and Guangdong tiles are the same as the memorial hall: I will not repeat them here.

III. Conclusion

For all the above projects, our factory has spared no expense and strived for perfection; if there is any slight impropriety, we will find a way to replace or redo it. Because the Central Government sincerely commemorates the burial place of loyal souls; our factory is also a member of the people, and we should understand the Central Government's supreme intention to comfort the heroic souls of the martyrs; and we dare not act rashly. Now that the great work has been completed, the construction process is described in detail on the right.

US Government Encourages Construction 208

— Geng Longgen

The United States government has always attached great importance to domestic construction; just looking at the development of the construction industry in the United States, which ranks first in the world, one can imagine that the United States government, on the one hand, spends huge amounts of money to build buildings that have an impact on society, and on the other hand, does its best to help and encourage people to build. Since the Democratic Party came to power, it has made even greater efforts for this policy. The most noteworthy thing is the two things done last summer—organizing a Federal Building Management Office and announcing the revised New Building Regulations.

The work of the Federal Building Management Office is to implement the will of the New Building Regulations, and to provide people with full economic and technical assistance when building houses. The administrator is Mr. Moffett J.S. Moffett. The office has been established for one year and has achieved considerable results. (According to reports, Mr. Moffett is a confidant of President Roosevelt; in early summer of this year, he was entrusted by President Roosevelt to come to Shanghai to conduct an informal investigation of the current situation of Chinese silver and the construction industry.)

The Federal Building Management Office not only helps people build new houses, but also helps with the repair and renovation of old houses. When the office was founded, administrator Moffett told reporters: There are 13 million houses in the United States that need repair, and 3 million houses that need minor repair. We hope to find ways to help these homeowners borrow money from their local financial institutions in the near future to improve their houses and make them safe and comfortable to live in.

The Federal Building Management Office does not directly lend money to the people. The Federal Building Management Office only helps the people contact many financial institutions to establish construction mortgage loans, and tries to protect the lenders' money.

Because of the different uses, this type of construction mortgage loan is divided into two types: one is for those who build new houses, and the other is for those who repair or renovate old houses. The amount of loans for building new houses can be borrowed up to 16,000 yuan, and the amount for repairing old houses ranges from 100 yuan to 2,000 yuan. The collateral is the house and real estate for which the loan is sought. Unless it violates national laws, there is no need for a guarantor. The interest rate is mostly 5%, but it may increase to 6% due to local conditions, plus an insurance fee of half a percent or one percent. The repayment method is in installments, and the repayment period can be as long as 20 years.

The method of borrowing money is quite easy. The borrower first asks an architect to estimate the amount of money needed, and then takes this estimate to a financial institution that establishes or manages this type of loan in the local area to request a loan. If this estimate is reviewed and approved, the required money can be borrowed. The procedure is simple, without any bureaucratic red tape.

Repayment by monthly installments is the most common. Each time the money is repaid, in addition to the principal and interest, an insurance fee of half a percent or one percent must be paid. The lender insures the borrower's house on their behalf. In the event of an accident in the borrower's house, the borrower can get compensation from the insurance company, and the lender can avoid losses.

If the borrower fails to repay the loan, the lender can request the Federal Building Management Office to use the power of the state to order the borrower to repay.

Since the establishment of the Federal Building Management Office and the promulgation of the revised New Building Regulations last year, the businesses of architects, material merchants, etc. that are directly related to construction have made a lot of progress.

There are also several commercial banks in our country that have established construction loans. I hope the government can help popularize this type of business.

The Gate and Fence of a Residence (Part 2) 209

— Hengyou Pan, translated by Chen Yin

(Continued from the Japanese supplement on page 10 of this newspaper on the 23rd)

Judging from today's social conditions or architectural styles, a somewhat open garden is more necessary than the non-open gardens of the past. If it is only to clearly separate the outside and the inside, or to prevent children and domestic animals from recklessly entering and leaving, then it can be said to be perfect. However, this hope may be too demanding. Here, for the design of the fence, firstly, the combination of appearance and practicality is very important.

Secondly, it is important to maintain harmony with the architecture and garden. For example, colored tiles, mudstone, and thatched Western-style buildings are completely incompatible with pure Japanese-style canopy doors or boat-board fences. Similarly, no matter how strong pure Japanese-style shoin-zukuri or teahouse-zukuri is, it is also discordant and unbalanced to use heavy and uninteresting brickwork or concrete construction. Also, in a larger sense, it is better for solemn buildings to be low and subdued, similarly, it is not good for tall buildings to be too low, as if they are sinking.

As for the choice of materials, it must also be carefully considered. There are many materials used for gates and fences in general residences, such as concrete, brick, iron, wood, and trees, etc., but these materials each have their own advantages and disadvantages depending on their location, architecture, garden, and economic conditions, so it is impossible to determine which is the best. However, in general, the materials for gates and fences must meet the necessary conditions. That is, they are economical, durable, and must have a beautiful appearance. From this point of view, ordinary hedges are the most ideal material. Building hedges is relatively cheap, the style is well-organized, they are durable, and they are more harmonious with any architecture and garden, and they have four seasons of changes, which other materials cannot match.

However, other materials also have their uses and their advantages, and to some extent, their shortcomings can be compensated for, so the most economical and closest one should be sought in the local area.
